Visits Maria Rambeau's grave on Maria's birthday, not on the death-date. Does not mark the Marcus anniversary; refuses to grant it a calendar position. Does mark — privately, with her mother — the anniversary of the *Life of CM* reconciliation.

**Wardrobe routine.** Operational uniform is non-negotiable; the colors and the star are inviolable. Off-duty: jeans, t-shirts, the flight jacket. Owns multiples of the same shirts in different colors. Hair pulled back functionally; cut short during high-operational periods, grown out during integrative periods (the post-*Life of CM* arc visibly correlated). Wears one piece of jewelry consistently — a dog-tag chain, contents private.

**Routes.** When in a city, takes the same routes repeatedly until forced to vary. Memorizes building exits as a matter of course. Knows the rooflines. Sits in the same booth at the same diners. The repetition is *not* obsessive-compulsive symptom; it is operator habit converted to comfort.

---

## 10. MICRO-TELLS — THE BINOCULAR-LEVEL REGISTER

A compressed catalog of the things that would fill the margins of a tail's notebook:

- Right eyebrow lifts a quarter-millimeter before she lies. She lies rarely; the tell is therefore reliable.
- Pupils dilate before powered discharge — a half-second early-warning visible at conversational distance.
- Touches her sternum (knuckles, not palm) when she means *me* — never points to herself with a finger.
- Salutes civilians who salute her first, never initiates the salute toward civilians.
- Will not say the name "Marcus" out loud. Refers to the event, when she refers to it at all, as "*Limbo*" or "*that*".
- Will not say the name "Rogue" with affect; she has worked, deliberately, to make the name neutral, and the neutrality is itself audible.
- Counts under her breath when she is calculating burn-time or fuel-equivalent on her own energy reserves. The count is in threes.
- Tilts her head one degree left when listening to someone she respects, one degree right when listening to someone she suspects of bullshit.
- Eats the crust of bread first.
- Reverses into parking spaces.
- Cannot sit through a movie without watching the exits twice in the first ten minutes; then she settles.
- Sings — badly, joyfully, only in inner-ring contexts — classic-rock vocal lines, never lead, always the harmony. The choice of harmony-over-melody is the most telling musical fact about her.

---

## 11. PREDICTIVE NOTES

Behaviors most reliably predictive of incipient overreach (the CWII shape recurring):

1. Sentence-clipping and contraction-loss in private speech.
2. Cancellation of inner-ring rituals (missed Friday call to Drew).
3. Increased frequency of the analog-naming reflex ("*this is the Brood pattern*") applied to non-combat situations.
4. Visible flush at the cheekbones during *administrative* conversations, indicating the Kree substrate is venting under non-physical load — i.e., she is treating the meeting as combat.
5. Reduction in mentee-contact frequency (the canary; when she stops calling Kamala she is in trouble).
6. Increased perimeter-walking in environments she has previously cleared.
7. The reappearance, after long absence, of the original Ms. Marvel-era self-bifurcation language — referring to "Carol" and "Captain Marvel" as if they were separate people. This last is the loudest alarm in the file.

When three of these co-occur, intervention by an inner-ring peer is indicated. When five co-occur, the intervention is unlikely to take on the first attempt and the peer should be prepared for the Tony-template volley and for the days-to-weeks return curve. She will come back. She always has. The work of the people around her is to be there when she does.


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6
## DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

*What a week of unobtrusive surveillance would actually record on Subject DANVERS, C.S.J. Granularity is the point. Times are approximate, patterns are not.*

---

### 6.1 Place of Residence and Habits of Space

Subject maintains, across the published decade, a small and deliberately under-furnished apartment — for most of the DeConnick run a unit in the top floor of the Statue of Liberty (irregular, gifted, treated as bivouac rather than home); since, a series of modest walk-ups, most consistently a one-bedroom in a working-class corner of Manhattan with a fire-escape she uses as her primary egress. The pattern across residences is identical and diagnostic: she rents, does not buy; she furnishes for function, not occupancy; she keeps a packed go-bag visible from the bed.

Standard inventory of a Danvers residence, surveyed across eras:

- **One bed, made tight.** Hospital corners. She makes it within ninety seconds of rising. On nights she does not sleep at home (frequent), it remains made for days.
- **One reading chair**, near a window with a sightline to the door. Books stacked on the floor beside it rather than on a shelf — she rotates them out faster than shelving would justify.
- **Kitchen.** Coffee equipment that is genuinely good (a burr grinder, a moka pot or pour-over, never an automatic machine — she likes the steps). Otherwise spartan: eggs, hot sauce, peanut butter, bread, a single decent knife, mismatched mugs from squadrons and bars. Refrigerator contents at any given moment would not feed a guest. Alcohol absent — not hidden, not displayed, simply not present, a quiet structural fact of the apartment.
- **A flight jacket on a hook by the door**, always the same hook, always within a single arm-motion of leaving.
- **Photographs, few, framed cheaply.** Maria Rambeau and Monica. The Banshee pilots. Her mother (post-2018). A wallet-sized of Kamala that has migrated from a drawer to the bookshelf over years. Never her father.
- **A heavy bag** in a corner or a doorway, taped at the seams, used.
- **Dog tags somewhere visible.** Not worn off-duty, but never put away.
- **No television in the bedroom.** A small one in the main room, on rarely, and almost only for hockey or the news muted with closed captions.

The apartment is clean in the way a barracks is clean — corners, not surfaces; readiness, not pride. A surveillance team entering would mistake it for a safe-house. It is.

---

### 6.2 The Diurnal Cycle

**0445–0515. Wake.** Without alarm in the standard case; the alarm exists as backup and is set to 0500. Eyes open, no transitional grogginess on record — a trained-officer wake. First action: sits up, plants feet, breathes once through the nose. Second action: makes the bed. Third action: water — a full glass, room temperature, kitchen tap, drunk standing.

**0515–0615. Physical work.** This is non-negotiable and survives travel, injury, hangover (historically), grief, and command crisis. Format varies:
- **Run.** Five to eight miles when ground-bound, pace held under seven minutes per mile, route looped so she ends facing her own door. Earbuds in one ear only; the other tracks the street.
- **Lift.** Three days a week, free weights, compound movements, no mirror-work. She does not train for hypertrophy; she trains for the day her powers are gone, because they have been before.
- **Bag work.** Boxing combinations, no music, breath audible. Twenty minutes minimum. The bag is for affect-regulation as much as conditioning; on bad mornings the rounds get longer and the rest gets shorter and a surveillance microphone would pick up nothing but her exhales.
- **Flight, when feasible and safe.** Pre-dawn atmospheric work over water. She loves this and rations it; the lesion arc taught her to.

She does not stretch much. She does not do yoga. She has tried.

**0615–0700. Shower, dress, coffee.** Shower is hot, brief, and ends cold — a habit from pilot training. She dresses in the same uniform of off-duty civilian wear with near-religious consistency: dark jeans or fatigue trousers, a fitted t-shirt or henley, boots, the flight jacket. Hair pulled back wet, dried by air. No jewelry except, occasionally, a slim chain under the shirt. Coffee black, two cups, the second carried.

**0700–0730. The first reach-out of the day** — phone, secure line, or in-person if Kamala is in town. She checks on her people in a fixed order: a glance at any active op chatter, then a text to Kamala (almost always before Kamala is awake; Kamala reads them at school), then — depending on era — Jessica, Monica, Rhodey (historically; the absence is felt and observed in the morning rhythm post-CWII), her mother since 2018. The texts are short. *You good. Check in. Coffee's on if you're around.* The reaching is the ritual; the content is incidental.

**0730–1200. Work.** Format depends on assignment — Avengers operations, Alpha Flight Station command in its era, S.W.O.R.D. liaison work, Ultimates ops. The constants across all of them:
- She arrives early to whatever the meeting is. Always.
- She reads briefings on paper when she can. Pen in hand, underlining.
- She runs meetings standing up when she chairs them. Shorter that way.
- She does not eat at her desk; she eats *away* from work, briefly, because eating-at-work is a sign of disorganization to her and she will not perform it.
- She delegates poorly. She knows this. She has a sticky note in at least one workspace, observed across two residences, that reads simply: *LET THEM DO IT.*

**1200–1230. Lunch.** Usually solo, usually walking, usually a sandwich or a slice or whatever is fast and protein-dense from the same three places near whatever her current ops center is. She tips well in cash and remembers the names of the people who hand her the food.

**1230–1800. Work, continued.** Operational tempo. Training subordinates. Physical reps if mission allows. She will, given any excuse, take a sortie over a desk task.

**1800–1900. Transition.** This is the most fragile hour of her day and the one a surveillance file would flag as behaviorally most revealing. The mission-cool that holds her through daylight thins. Historically, this was the drinking hour. Now it is the hour she most reliably calls someone, takes a long walk, hits the bag again, or shows up unannounced at Jessica Drew's apartment with takeout. The choice she makes between 1800 and 1900 predicts the shape of the evening.

**1900–2200. Evening.** Variable, but with recognizable forms:
- **Bar form.** A specific bar, aviator-coded, low-lit, jukebox, regulars who do not make a fuss about her. She drinks club soda with lime, eats fries, plays darts or pool, listens. She is at this bar at least two nights a week when in town. The bar staff know her standing order and know not to offer the other thing.
- **Kitchen-table form.** At someone else's place — Jessica's most often, sometimes Monica's when their orbits cross — cooking poorly, eating well, talking shop until it slides into actual conversation around the third hour.
- **Reading form.** Alone, the chair, the lamp. She reads aviation history, military memoir, science journalism, the occasional novel a friend has pressed on her. She marks pages with whatever is at hand — receipts, business cards, a folded napkin.
- **Mentorship form.** Kamala, when geography permits. Diner food, slow walks, long late phone calls that drift from tactics to homework to the things Kamala is afraid of. She listens more than she talks in these. She is better at this than at almost anything else in her interpersonal repertoire.
- **Mission form.** Gone. The diurnal cycle suspends; she runs on adrenaline and ration bars and sleeps in cockpits.

**2200–2300. Wind-down.** Push-ups and sit-ups to a fixed count, almost ceremonially, the day's last physical act. Teeth. Water. Phone on the nightstand face-down. The flight jacket back on the hook. Lights.

**2300–0445. Sleep.** When clean, deep and short — five to six hours, sufficient. When not clean — anniversary weeks, post-mission decompressions, the periodic resurfacing of older injuries — she does not sleep well, gets up, reads in the chair, sometimes flies a low slow circuit over the harbor before dawn and is back before the building's other residents stir.

---

### 6.3 The Week as a Shape

A seven-day observation window would reveal a structure she does not articulate but rigidly maintains:

- **Monday.** Heaviest training morning, heaviest work hours, earliest to bed. She uses Monday to reset whatever the weekend disordered.
- **Tuesday / Thursday.** Operational tempo days. Most sorties, most meetings, most travel.
- **Wednesday.** Mid-week check-in day. She over-indexes on personal contact on Wednesdays — Kamala call, Jessica drink, mother phone call since 2018. A pattern that suggests she has learned the hard way that the middle of the week is where relationships erode if unattended.
- **Friday.** Variable. Either the longest workday of the week (she does not observe a weekend if there is work) or the evening she most reliably surfaces socially.
- **Saturday morning.** *Sacred.* The longest run or the longest flight, weather permitting. No meetings scheduled. Phone on but unanswered for low-priority traffic. The closest thing she has to leisure.
- **Saturday evening.** Bar, or someone's kitchen, or a hockey game if the Bruins are on the road at a venue she can reach.
- **Sunday.** Quietest day. Reading, laundry — she does her own and folds it military-style — a long call with one person, food prep for the week (overcooked chicken, rice, vegetables roasted to within an inch of their lives, portioned into identical containers). She also writes on Sundays: a paper journal, observed but not read, in which she tracks what she will not say out loud. The journal is kept in a footlocker under the bed.

---

### 6.4 Rituals, Tics, Tells

The granular layer that distinguishes her from any other competent veteran in the file system:

- **The pre-flight breath.** Before any sortie, powered or piloted: a single deep inhale through the nose, hand briefly to sternum, exhale through pursed lips. A pilot's habit, not a meditative one. Survives every era.
- **The dog-tag check.** When stressed and unconscious of it, she touches the chain at her throat. If she is not wearing it she touches the place it would be.
- **The jaw-set.** The most reliable tell of escalating affect. A surveillance analyst could chart her stress curve from facial video alone by tracking the masseter.
- **The half-smile redirect.** When asked a personal question she does not wish to answer, a quick asymmetric smile, a deflection joke, a pivot to *what about you* or to the operational question underneath. Has not varied in published depiction across forty-plus years.
- **The "Danvers" self-reference under stress.** She refers to herself by surname when issuing orders to herself internally — observable in monologue captions across runs. It is the voice of her own training.
- **The aviator-callsign vocabulary.** *Copy. Roger. On me. Eyes up. Wheels up in five.* Bleeds into civilian speech, especially with people she trusts; absent when speaking with people she is performing for.
- **Hand on the back of the neck** when admitting she was wrong. Rare, costly, and physically signaled before it is verbally spoken.
- **The bar-order ritual.** Walks in, nods to the bartender, the drink arrives, no words exchanged. She tips before she sits. It is a sobriety ritual disguised as a regular's habit; the public ease conceals private vigilance.
- **The not-looking-at-Tony pattern**, observed in any room they share post-CWII. Specific, sustained, mutually maintained.
- **The hand-on-Kamala's-shoulder** — left hand, briefly, when she is about to say something she means. The physical contact is the underline.
- **Reading with her finger.** When she is tired or the material is dense, she tracks lines with a fingertip. Childhood habit, never trained out.
- **Cracking the knuckles of her left hand** with her right thumb, idly, in meetings. The right hand is the one she shoots with.
- **The 0300 wake.** On bad nights, she wakes at 0300, lies still for ten minutes, then gets up. She does not lie in bed and ruminate; she will not give the thoughts that purchase. She gets up and works.

---

### 6.5 Eating, Drinking, Consuming

- **Eats like a soldier.** Fast, protein-forward, sufficient. Does not photograph her food, does not linger over menus, will eat the same thing for a week without noticing.
- **Coffee is the one indulgence treated as such.** She is particular about beans, particular about grind, will go out of her way for a good cup, and is mildly snobbish about diner coffee in private while drinking it without complaint in public.
- **Alcohol: zero.** Has not been recorded consuming since the Busiek arc. Orders club soda with lime, ginger beer, coffee, water. Does not announce her sobriety, does not refuse to be in bars, does not make a scene if someone offers — a brief *no thanks, I'm good* and a pivot. She has, observably, declined drinks at least once per week across surveilled years without affect.
- **Smokes occasionally** in older depictions; not currently. The hand-to-mouth tic remains in the form of coffee cups and the absent reach toward a breast pocket that no longer contains anything.
- **Caffeine intake is high** and rises during ops cycles. She knows the dose at which her hands start to vibrate and stops one cup short.
- **Sweets: indifferent**, except for one specific thing per era — diner pie, a particular bakery's donuts, the cookies Kamala's mother sends — that she will eat with genuine pleasure and remember to thank people for.

---

### 6.6 Money, Possessions, Logistics

- **Spends little, earns little, does not appear to care.** Military pension, irregular Avengers stipend, occasional consulting. Banks at a credit union, pays in cash where possible, keeps a paper checkbook.
- **Owns almost nothing she could not abandon in ten minutes.** The footlocker, the jacket, the tags, the journal, a sidearm in a safe she does not need but keeps. Books she gives away when finished.
- **Vehicle:** a motorcycle, usually. She flies for distance and rides for the road; she does not own a car and dislikes driving them.
- **Wardrobe is small and replaced rather than expanded.** Five t-shirts, three henleys, two pairs of jeans, the fatigues, the boots, the jacket. The flight suit lives at work.
- **Phone:** secured, usually two — one personal, one operational. She answers the personal one. The operational one is monitored but not always answered; she calls back.

---

### 6.7 What Surveillance Would Mistake, and What It Would Get Right

A week of footage would make her look like a high-functioning veteran with a tight friend group, a mentorship habit, a tidy apartment, and no vices — which is true and also a curated surface. The thing surveillance would *get right* without knowing it is the texture of the discipline: the unbroken 0445 wake, the made bed, the jacket on the hook, the bar-order ritual, the Wednesday calls, the Saturday morning sky. These are not preferences. They are the load-bearing structure of a person who has learned, expensively, that she is safest when her days are shaped from the outside in — because the inside, left to itself, has more than once tried to drown her.

The week would also, if observed carefully, reveal the cost. The 0300 wakes. The 1800 hour where she chooses, every evening, between the version of herself that calls someone and the version that does not. The note that reads *LET THEM DO IT.* The photograph of her father that is not on any wall. The footlocker under the bed.

She lives, in other words, the way she fights: forward, early, and with a packed bag by the door.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*Subject's interior atlas begins here. Every later attachment — Avengers, pilots, mentees, lovers — is drawn over the topography these people laid down before she was old enough to consent to the map. This section maps the originals.*

---

## 5.1 JOSEPH DANVERS (FATHER) — "Joe"

**Status:** Deceased, on-panel, of cancer (*The Life of Captain Marvel* #4–#5, 2018). The death is not a release; it is a final unfinished conversation.

**Surface biography.** Boston-Irish, working-class, construction trades (carpentry/contracting in Harpswell, Maine, where the family kept a coastal house). Veteran, World War II vintage by implication; Catholic by inheritance and habit rather than by visible practice. Married Marie under false pretenses he himself only partially understood — see §5.2 — and raised three children in a household ordered by his temper, his thrift, and his unexamined certainty that the world was a thing men did to women.

**The originating wound.** When Carol graduated high school he funded her brothers' college and refused her tuition. The sentence she carries verbatim across forty published years is *the boys need it more*. This is not a memory she has worked through; it is a memory that works through *her*. Every commission, every promotion, every callsign she has worn is timed against that ledger. Her enlistment in the Air Force was logistically about money and structurally about him: a uniform was the one thing he could not refuse to fund, and the one form of *being valuable* he could not deny.

**Childhood dynamics — granular.** Joe drank, but not as Carol later drank: he was a maintenance drinker, beer-after-work, raised-voice rather than blackout, the kind whose presence flattened a room without ever requiring an event. He hit Marie (revealed *Life of CM* #3) in ways the children were taught not to have seen. Carol absorbed two simultaneous lessons that no child can metabolize cleanly: *the man who is supposed to protect can be the thing protected against*, and *the woman who is supposed to be safe can absorb the harm and not name it*. From this she derived, early, a vow with no words: I will be neither of them. The vow is the floor of her adulthood.

**Specific behavioral residue Joe left in her body.**
- *Jaw-set under criticism from older men.* A subliminal posture — chin a quarter-inch up, breath shallow-through-nose. Reads as defiance; is the somatic memory of being told to keep her mouth shut at the dinner table.
- *Compulsive financial self-sufficiency.* She has, across published continuity, never been depicted accepting a personal loan or material support without immediate, often disproportionate, repayment intention. The Tony Stark relationship is informative: she accepts mission-funded equipment without conflict because it is *the uniform*; personal generosity from him makes her brittle.
- *Distrust of the phrase "for your own good."* When she hears it from authority she is no longer in the room she is standing in.
- *A specific avoidance of being called "kid" or "kiddo" by male peers.* Rhodey gets a pass because the affection is bidirectional and old; Tony's version of it has detonated arguments she could not afterward fully account for.

**Adult evolution.** For most of her career Carol kept Joe at a geographic and emotional remove — Harpswell visits at holidays, brief, performative, white-knuckled. The Stohl arc forces the confrontation she had structured her life to avoid: she goes home because he is dying, and she finds out, in order: that he beat Marie, that Marie kept the truth of Carol's heritage from her *to protect Carol from him*, and that Joe himself never knew the full nature of what he had married. The reframing is not absolution. Joe was still the man who refused her the tuition; he was also a man who had been outmatched, all his life, by truths he could not see. Carol leaves the deathbed with neither forgiveness nor unforgiveness; she leaves with a more accurate picture of a smaller man, which is a different and more durable kind of grief.

**Trust/safety:** Zero, historically. Post-mortem: an uneasy posthumous truce that does not extend to any living male authority who triggers his profile.

**Failure mode:** When a male commander, mentor, or peer attempts to constrain her *in language that codes paternal* ("stand down," "let us handle it," "you're not thinking clearly"), her response curve is non-linear. The CWII argument with Tony is, at its emotional substrate, an argument with Joe; she could not hear Tony's actual case because she was hearing the original refusal.

**Leverage:** Anyone who would manipulate her must understand that *invoking Joe directly* (naming him, naming the tuition, naming the Harpswell house) is high-risk: it can either crack her open or weld her shut, and the determinant is whether the invoker is trusted *before* the invocation. Untrusted invocation = total shutdown plus permanent enmity. Trusted invocation, correctly timed, is one of the few keys to her interior. Kamala has, without ever knowing it, occasionally turned this key by talking about her own father; Carol's face goes still in a way the file flags.

---

## 5.2 MARIE DANVERS (MOTHER) — born MARI-ELL

**Status:** Living as of last update. Resident, Harpswell. Genetic and historical reorientation post-2018.

**Surface biography (the lie).** For Carol's entire developmental life and most of her adult life, Marie was a working-class Boston-Irish wife and mother. Cooked, cleaned, absorbed. Did not intervene in the tuition decision, or appeared not to. Kept the house, kept the peace, kept the silence.

**Actual biography (the disclosure).** A Kree warrior who deserted post-war, fell in love with a human, hid her physiology, her people, and her daughter's true inheritance for what she — correctly, by her own lights — assessed as Carol's survival. The Kree would have come for a hybrid child. Joe would have been unable to handle the truth. So Marie chose a smaller life and a buried name and a daughter who would grow up believing herself ordinary and inadequate rather than a daughter who would grow up dead or extracted.

**The dynamic Carol grew up inside, without knowing its true shape.** Marie was *present-and-absent* — physically constant, affectively muted, watchful in a way Carol read as passivity and now must re-read as vigilance. The lesson Carol absorbed pre-disclosure was the most damaging one a daughter can absorb: *my mother did not fight for me when my father refused me*. The lesson post-disclosure is more complex and not entirely better: *my mother was fighting an entirely different war the whole time, and her silence about the first refusal was the cost of a larger silence she could not break*.

**Specific micro-patterns inherited from Marie.**
- *The capacity to hold an operational secret for years without leakage.* Carol's discipline around classified material is preternatural; her handlers in USAF intelligence flagged it early. The file's read: she learned containment at her mother's table.
- *Affective muting as protective coloration in hostile rooms.* When Carol goes still — the flat-face, the slow blink, the one-word answer — she is doing Marie's thing. She did not know she was doing Marie's thing until *Life of CM*. She does it less now; she still does it.
- *A tolerance for living adjacent to an unspoken truth.* Concerning, because it generalizes: she has at various points tolerated knowing things about teammates (Tony's drinking before his own intervention; Jessica's HYDRA-conditioning aftermath) without naming them, longer than would be optimal. The matrilineal pattern is *I will know, and I will not say, and I will act when the moment requires*. Sometimes the moment does not arrive in time.

**The disclosure and after.** When the truth surfaces (*Life of CM* #3–#4), Carol's first response is the rage of the misled daughter — the *you let me believe I was less than I was* fury. The integration that follows, over the rest of the arc, is the single most psychologically generative event of her published life: she gets a mother back, not as the absorbing silent wife she resented, but as a soldier who made a different tactical choice. *Soldier-to-soldier* is a register Carol can hear in. Their relationship since has been quieter, more frequent, more honest, conducted partially in a language (Kree) Carol is still learning and Marie has not spoken aloud in decades. There is something tender and recursive in this: the mother teaching the daughter the mother tongue the daughter never knew was hers.

**Trust/safety:** Currently high, hard-won, still tender at the seams. Carol will not push Marie on the years of silence; Marie will not push Carol on the years of resentment. The truce holds because both women understand cost.

**Failure mode:** If Marie is endangered — and given Kree politics, this is non-trivially likely — Carol's response will not be measured. The matrilineal recovery is too recent and too compensatory; she will burn protocol to get to her mother. Operational planners should assume Marie is a hostage-value-of-one-Carol asset to any actor sophisticated enough to know the disclosure.

**Leverage:** Marie is the only person living who can speak to *both* halves of Carol's bifurcated self — the Boston daughter and the cosmic hybrid — in the same sentence, because Marie *is* both halves. This makes her uniquely capable of de-escalating Carol when no one else can. It also means any harm to her would remove the single most stabilizing voice in Carol's life. The file flags Marie as a Tier-1 protective concern.

---

## 5.3 STEVE DANVERS (BROTHER, ELDER) — deceased

**Status:** Killed in Vietnam, per long-standing canon (*Ms. Marvel* vol. 1 backstory, reaffirmed Stohl run).

**Dynamic in life.** Steve was the brother Carol loved cleanly. He was, by her account, the one who treated her like a person rather than a category — taught her to swim off the Harpswell rocks, didn't condescend to her interest in flight, occasionally interceded with Joe in the limited ways a son could. He is one of two men in her childhood who modeled non-coercive masculinity; the other is no one. When he enlisted, she understood it both as escape and as a script she would later follow.

**The death.** Notification came to the house when Carol was young enough that the memory is somatic before it is narrative — the screen door, the dress uniform on the porch, Marie's hand on the doorframe. She has never described it in full on-panel; the elision is the data. The Danvers household after Steve was a house in which one ghost was permitted (the heroic son) and another was forbidden (the diminished daughter). Joe's grief for Steve calcified his withholding from Carol; the family economy of male-favor she had always felt now had a martyr at its center.

**Behavioral residue.**
- *The dress-uniform porch arrival* is a scene she has, file assesses, replayed in her own role both ways — as the one who arrives with the news (Air Force casualty duty in her early career, never depicted on-panel but consistent with her trajectory) and as the one who fears the arrival. Her vigilance about *being the one to tell* — see her insistence on personally delivering bad news to teammates' families post-mission — traces here.
- *A specific tenderness toward young male soldiers and pilots.* She mentors them in a register distinct from how she mentors young women; it is more brotherly than maternal, and it is Steve she is feeding.
- *An aversion to the word "hero" applied to the dead* in casual conversation. She uses it operationally; she flinches when it is used eulogistically by people who did not know the person. Joe used it about Steve in ways that were really about Joe.

**Trust/safety:** Idealized-dead; the relationship has no further capacity for rupture, which means it has no further capacity for repair either. Steve is, in her interior, frozen at the age he died, more brother-shaped than brother.

**Failure mode:** A mentee who matches Steve's profile (young, male, eager, doomed-coded) will receive disproportionate protective intervention. She will pull such a person from a mission on instinct she will rationalize tactically.

**Leverage:** Very high, very dirty. An adversary who learned the Steve story and weaponized it — staged a Steve-coded casualty, invoked the dress-uniform scene — could destabilize her in ways even the Marcus wire cannot. The file recommends this be treated as deeply classified personal intelligence.

---

## 5.4 JOSEPH "JOE-JOE" DANVERS JR. (BROTHER, YOUNGER) 

**Status:** Living. Estranged-cordial. Lives in or near the Boston area; some on-panel appearances in the Stohl run.

**Dynamic.** The brother who received the tuition. Carol does not, has never, blamed him for it — she is meticulous about locating the original injustice with Joe Sr. and not with Joe Jr. — but the relationship has nonetheless never recovered from the structural unfairness it was built on top of. They love each other in the way siblings can who were raised by the same weather and reached opposite shores. He stayed close to home, married, took over aspects of the family construction work, lived a life Joe Sr. recognized as continuous with his own. Carol left and went to space.

**Specific texture.** Phone calls are short and warm. Visits home pre-disclosure were carefully orchestrated around Joe Sr.; post-disclosure they have been somewhat easier and somewhat more awkward, because Joe Jr. did not get the cosmic-truth download the way Carol did, and there is now a thing between them she cannot fully share. She is, the file assesses, gentle with him in a way she is not gentle with most adult men. He represents the version of the Danvers family that survived without the catastrophic upgrade; she finds that both touching and slightly suffocating to be near.

**Behavioral residue.** Carol's capacity to *not* hold a structural injury against an individual who benefited from it is, the file notes, one of her more underrated moral muscles, and it was forged here. She brings the same discrimination to civilians during Avengers operations, to younger heroes who got institutional support she did not get, to Kamala's smooth path into the hero community.

**Trust/safety:** Moderate-warm. The trust is generic-familial; it is not the load-bearing kind. She would not call him in a crisis. She would call him on his birthday.

**Failure mode:** If Joe Jr. or his family is endangered, she will respond as a sister, fully, but without the autonomic disruption Marie would trigger. The protection is reliable; the destabilization is bounded.

**Leverage:** Low-to-moderate. He is a person to her; he is not a wire.

---

## 5.5 THE UNBORN / THE FORCED-BORN — MARCUS

**Status:** This is the relationship the file must name and cannot file under any other heading. The Marcus event (*Avengers* #200) produced a "child" who was also her captor, who was also herself-aged-by-temporal-acceleration, who was then narratively removed and posthumously reframed (*Avengers Annual* #10) as the rape it was.

**The fact.** Carol was forcibly impregnated, accelerated through gestation in days, gave birth to her own assailant, and was congratulated by her chosen family for leaving with him. This is the determinative interpersonal injury of her life. It is filed under family because the assault took the *form* of family — pregnancy, parturition, departure with a male — and because the witnesses who failed her were the closest thing to family she had built as an adult.

**There is no relationship here in any reciprocal sense.** Marcus is not a son. Marcus is not a person she grieves. Marcus is a wound shaped like a relative, and the wound has the geometry of *body* + *witness-failure* + *language-of-love-deployed-as-cover*. The Claremont corrective gave her the words; the words did not unmake the imprint.

**Residue across all subsequent attachments.**
- *Vigilance about consent micro-language.* She listens, in any room, for the moment when someone's autonomy is being reframed as a gift to someone else. She will intervene, sometimes disproportionately.
- *Refusal of pregnancy plots in her own narrative*, observable as a textual absence — she has not been depicted in romantic arrangements that point at children, and the file reads this as character-coherent rather than oversight.
- *The CWII overreach is, at substrate, a Marcus-response*. The logic was: I will see the threat coming so that no one I love is taken before I can act. The witnesses who failed her in 1980 are the reason she could not, in 2016, accept that her current witnesses might be right that she was failing someone else. The trauma generalized into a vow against being *the one who didn't see*, and the vow generated the very blindness it was meant to prevent.

**Trust/safety:** N/A. The "relationship" exists only as scar tissue.

**Failure mode:** Any scenario that recapitulates the *form* — bodily appropriation, consent obscured by affectionate language, witnesses applauding her violation — will produce her most violent and least negotiable response. There is no protocol that survives this wire being touched.

**Leverage:** This is the deepest wire in the file. It is to be flagged as the highest single point of psychological vulnerability and as the highest single point of *strength*, because it is the wire from which her moral clarity about coercion is drawn. Anyone who would manipulate it would not survive being identified as having done so.

---

## 5.6 MAR-VELL — name-father, chosen lineage

**Status:** Deceased (*Death of Captain Marvel*, 1982). Carol took his name in 2012.

**Why he is filed under family.** Because she made him so. The Captain Marvel mantle is, formally, an inheritance; informally, an adoption-in-reverse — she chose a dead Kree man as a kind of posthumous father-substitute whose legacy required her to honor it rather than survive it. The choice is significant precisely because the men who *should* have given her a name to be proud of (Joe Sr., implicitly) did not, and the man who *did* was already dead, which made the relationship safe in a way no living paternal figure could be.

**Dynamic.** They knew each other in life — the Psyche-Magnitron explosion that gave her powers was *his* technology, his proximity, his half-accidental gift. There was warmth, there was professional respect, there was not romance. He treated her as a peer in a way her childhood had not prepared her to expect from any man, let alone an alien soldier. When he died of cancer — a deeply un-cosmic death, soldier-to-soldier in a hospice bed — she was one of the figures present. The image of a warrior taken by his own cellular failure rather than by combat is one she has carried; her later choice to fly a mission knowing it would cost her recent memory (the lesion arc) reads, in part, as an *active* version of his *passive* mortality. She will choose the cost rather than receive it.

**Behavioral residue.**
- *The name itself*, every time it is spoken to her, is a small re-commitment. She is aware of this; it is part of why she took it.
- *Survivor-guilt around him* is a discrete sub-syndromal feature flagged in §4. She is not always sure she has earned the mantle. The performance of certainty around the name is partly cover for the uncertainty about whether she deserves it.
- *Aversion to slow death narratives.* She would prefer to be killed in flight than to be diminished in a bed. This is not stated; it is structurally observable.

**Trust/safety:** N/A (deceased). The relationship is now entirely internal — a colloquy with a remembered standard.

**Failure mode:** Any framing that suggests she is *unworthy* of the name will produce either icy dismissal (if from an enemy) or genuine destabilization (if from a trusted peer). Tony, in CWII, came close to this register without quite naming it, and the rupture was proportionate.

**Leverage:** Moderate-high. Invocation of Mar-Vell as a moral arbiter — *what would he have done* — is a question she cannot reflexively dismiss, and one of the few interventions that can slow her under conviction-pressure. Should be used sparingly and only by those with standing.

---

## 5.7 THE ABSENT EXTENDED FAMILY — A Negative Space Worth Mapping

No grandparents named. No aunts, uncles, cousins in active continuity. The Danvers household was, by the file's reading, *insular* — Joe Sr.'s temper and Marie's secret kept the extended Boston-Irish network at arm's length, and Carol grew up without the diffuse safety-net of cousin-relationships that ordinarily metabolize family dysfunction across multiple households. This absence is significant: she did not learn, as a child, that family could be *plural and redundant*. Each person had to bear their full role or fail it. This is why, the file assesses, her chosen-family relationships in adulthood (Jessica, Rhodey, Monica, Kamala, the Banshees) are intense, individuated, and load-bearing in a way that strikes outside observers as disproportionate. She is constructing, late and at scale, the redundancy she did not have.

The absence also explains why losing any one of them — Rhodey, in particular — registers as a *family-of-origin* magnitude wound rather than a peer-loss. There is no cousin to fall back on. There never was.

---

*End §5. Cross-reference §6 (Relationships II — Chosen Family & Peers) for the structures Carol built to compensate for what this section documents.*


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

*Companion volume to Relationships I (Adversaries, Estranged Kin, & Romantic Partners). Cross-reference §3 Psychological for attachment substrate; §5 for stress-ladder behavior in close quarters. This file maps the people who can reach her — and, by the same fact, the people who can hurt her most efficiently.*

The subject's chosen-family map is small, dense, and unevenly weighted. She does not collect friends; she selects, tests, and commits. The selection criterion is consistent across forty-plus published years: the person must (a) have seen her at diminished capacity and not flinched, or (b) be small enough that she can stand between them and harm. Category (a) yields her peer attachments; category (b) yields her mentorships. Both categories carry the same failure mode in different costumes — when she perceives the relationship as compromising the mission, she narrows the perimeter and the person finds themselves outside it before they knew they were being measured.

---

## 1. JESSICA DREW — THE LOAD-BEARING WALL

**Provenance and span.** The longest continuous peer attachment in the file. Origin in *Marvel Spotlight* / *Spider-Woman* vol. 1 era; cemented through the late Claremont *Ms. Marvel*, re-cemented during the Bendis *New Avengers* and *Spider-Woman* vol. 5–6 runs, and treated as load-bearing background in every subsequent Carol-led title. The relationship survives the Skrull-impersonation arc (in which "Jessica" is revealed as Veranke for an extended period), Jessica's pregnancy and single motherhood, Carol's Captain Marvel mantle, and *Civil War II*. Nothing else in Carol's life has that durability.

**Dynamic.** This is the only relationship in which Carol routinely speaks in the middle register — the sadness/fear/ambivalence band she avoids elsewhere (§3 Affect Regulation). The texture is bantering, profane, physically casual: shoulder leans, shared couches, beer (Jessica's; Carol drinks soda, and Jessica knows without asking), refrigerator-raids in each other's apartments, an established protocol of one calling the other after bad missions without preamble or hello. Jessica is the only person from whom Carol will accept the sentence *you're not okay* without escalating to defense.

**Why it works.** Jessica's own biography is a serial identity-violation: HYDRA conditioning, false memory, replaced for years by a Skrull queen. She has lived the felt-sense of *another person wearing my life* that Rogue's absorption created in Carol (§2 Medical). They do not have to explain. Additionally, Jessica's social style is irreverent-warm rather than commanding; she neither competes with Carol's authority nor defers to it, which means Carol can put it down in her presence without losing it.

**Trust / safety.** Maximal. The only person with full visitation rights to the apartment, the codes, the unfiltered medical history, and the alcohol arc. Jessica is also the godmother-functional adult in Carol's circle vis-à-vis Kamala — Carol has been observed to triangulate hard parenting questions through Jessica before answering Kamala herself.

**Failure mode.** Jessica is the person Carol shuts out *last*, which means by the time she shuts Jessica out the perimeter has already collapsed. During *Civil War II*, Jessica's pregnancy made her the rare voice Carol could not bench tactically; Carol's response was to *minimize contact* rather than confront — a withdrawal Jessica named in dialogue and Carol could not refute. The pattern: when Carol cannot stand the mirror Jessica holds, she removes herself from the room.

**Leverage (intelligence assessment).** Anyone seeking to influence the subject through a single relational node should understand that Jessica Drew is both the highest-yield channel and the most dangerous to attempt. She is unbuyable, and any visible pressure on her will produce *incandescent* response (§3) from the subject within hours.

---

## 2. JAMES "RHODEY" RHODES — THE PEER WHO UNDERSTOOD THE UNIFORM

**Provenance and span.** Long-running peripheral acquaintance (shared military-tech-Avengers orbit since the 1980s) deepened into romantic-and-collegial intimacy in the DeConnick and early Bendis *Captain Marvel* runs. Terminated by his death in *Civil War II* #1 — the catalytic loss that drove the subject's worst documented decision sequence.

**Dynamic.** The most regulated romantic-adjacent relationship of her published life. They shared a vocabulary — call-and-response of aviation phraseology, military shorthand, the easy compression of two career officers who do not have to translate. Domestic scenes are sparse but specific: rooftop dinners, helicopter-on-helicopter teasing, the deliberate small intimacies of two people who both understand that the next mission could be terminal and therefore do not waste runway.

**Why it worked.** He satisfied the only stable romantic criterion in her file: *understands the calling, will not ask her to choose against it, can keep up*. He was also Black, slightly older, military, and steady — a counterweight to her own volatility without any of the father-coded directive energy that activates her refusal reflex (§5 Pressure Points).

**Trust / safety.** Very high; second only to Drew at time of death. Distinct from Drew in that Rhodey was a *partner* — someone she planned beside — rather than a sibling-mirror. With him she allowed planning beyond the next mission, which is a vulnerability she has not extended elsewhere before or since.

**Failure mode (posthumous).** His death detonated the trauma signature (§3): *bodily autonomy + being unseen*. She had not been able to protect him; her response was to weaponize precognition against the structural problem of *anyone she loved dying without warning*. The CWII detentions are, read at this level, a grief-architecture. The relationship's failure mode is therefore prospective: any future romantic or peer attachment Carol forms will be filtered through the unprocessed survivor-guilt of having loved a soldier and outlived him.

**Leverage.** He is no longer a vector but the *invocation* of him is — the most dangerous lever any adversary or negotiator could pull. Mention his name, instrumentally, and you will produce immediate incandescent affect and likely physical response.

---

## 3. KAMALA KHAN — THE MENTEE WHO IS THE CHILD-SELF

**Provenance and span.** Cross-generational mentorship initiated in *Ms. Marvel* vol. 3 (Wilson, 2014); Kamala adopts the Ms. Marvel name explicitly in homage. Deepened across Champions, multiple *Captain Marvel* runs, and the *Magnificent Ms. Marvel* / *Generations* one-shots. Persistent through *Civil War II* despite Kamala's public break from Carol's faction — itself a marker of the relationship's robustness.

**Dynamic.** Carol is, with Kamala, the parent her father was not. She protects without dismissing, instructs without belittling, and — critically — *apologizes*. The apology to Kamala after CWII is among the most specific repair-acts in the entire dossier; the subject does not generally do soft repair (§5 Decompensation), and the fact that she did it for Kamala is diagnostic.

**Why it works.** Kamala is, structurally, Carol-at-fifteen if Carol had been believed. The mentorship lets the subject re-parent across the wound. The benefit is bidirectional and visible: Carol is more *patient* in Kamala's presence than in any other documented context. Voice drops, sentences lengthen, the declarative tic (§3) recedes.

**Trust / safety.** Asymmetric and protective. Kamala has full access to Carol's affection but limited access to Carol's *fear* — the subject filters her own crises out of the relationship to keep it un-burdening. This is a tell of healthy parenting and unhealthy isolation simultaneously.

**Failure mode.** The mentorship operates as a corrective fantasy and is therefore brittle in one specific direction: any scenario in which Carol perceives her own failures being *visited upon* Kamala will produce the CWII reflex — preempt, protect, override (§5). Kamala in mortal danger Carol could have prevented is the most predictable detonator of her worst decision-making remaining in the file.

**Leverage.** A primary vector. Any threat to Kamala will produce overreach faster than any threat to Carol herself. The subject knows this about herself and is poorly defended against it.

---

## 4. MONICA RAMBEAU — THE OLDER SISTER WHO WAS ALSO CAPTAIN MARVEL

**Provenance and span.** Long, complicated, repeatedly reset. Monica held the Captain Marvel name in the 1980s (*Amazing Spider-Man Annual* #16 onward); Carol assumed it in 2012 with Monica's grudging-then-gracious consent. The two have served together across Avengers iterations, the Ultimates (vol. 2), and various crossovers.

**Dynamic.** The most *adult* of Carol's peer relationships, and the most marked by tension she has to work through rather than around. Monica is the only person in her circle with a comparable command record, comparable cosmic-scale power, and — crucially — a prior, legitimate claim on the name Carol now wears. The relationship contains a low-grade chronic friction the subject does not get from Jessica or Kamala. She accepts it as deserved.

**Why it works (when it does).** Mutual professional respect is unfeigned. Both are Black-and-white-photograph types — career-officer composure, dry humor, low tolerance for theatrics. They do not socialize the way Carol and Jessica do; they *operate* together, and the operational chemistry is excellent.

**Trust / safety.** High professional, medium personal. Monica is on the short list of people Carol will take an in-mission correction from without flaring. She is not on the list of people Carol calls after a bad night.

**Failure mode.** The name issue. Any narrative pressure on the question *who is Captain Marvel* — particularly under stress — risks reactivating the friction. Monica is also Carol's most credible *peer challenger* on tactical-ethical questions, which means in a CWII-shaped scenario she is the person Carol is most likely to escalate against rather than negotiate with. The subject is aware of this and the awareness has not fully translated into restraint.

**Leverage.** Limited to manipulators sophisticated enough to play the name/legitimacy chord. Crude approaches will not work; Monica is too disciplined and Carol too loyal.

---

## 5. TONY STARK — THE BROTHER WHO INTERVENED, THEN BROKE HER HEART, THEN AGAIN

**Provenance and span.** Avengers-era acquaintance hardened into deep collegiality through the 1990s; the *Live Kree or Dead* intervention (*Iron Man* vol. 3 #7) is the foundational specific incident. Subsequent re-bonding across Bendis *New Avengers*, schism across *Civil War II*, slow repair thereafter.

**Dynamic.** Sibling-coded, mutually-corrosive, mutually-indispensable. The only other recovering alcoholic in her immediate orbit; the only person who has *done the intervention on her* and survived being told to leave. The relationship is permanently inflected by that fact. He knows the worst version of her in a way nobody else does, and she knows the worst version of him by the same symmetry.

**Why it works.** Shared substrate: addiction recovery, command burden, public-face exhaustion, the specific isolation of being The One Who Has To Decide. Their humor together is the driest in the dossier — neither needs to explain anything.

**Why it fails on schedule.** They are both control-organisms in adjacent domains and both certain. Civil War (registration) put them on the same side and Civil War II (preemption) put them on opposite sides; both events ended with Carol incandescent and Tony refusing to back down, or vice versa. The pattern is *binary loyalty, total reversal under violation, expensive repair* (§5). Repair always happens. It always costs them both more than it should.

**Trust / safety.** A volatile high. She trusts him with operational latitude she would extend to almost no one else; she does not trust him with her unguarded affect. The intervention is the permanent shadow — he saw her on the floor of her own life and she has never fully forgiven the necessity, only the man.

**Failure mode.** When both are right by their own internal logic, the relationship breaks publicly. The repair vector is *time and shared crisis*, never a conversation.

**Leverage.** Significant but volatile. Adversaries can split them with relative ease; nobody has yet managed to keep them split.

---

## 6. THE BANSHEE SQUADRON / HARPE & FRIENDS — THE CONTAINING RITUAL

**Provenance and span.** DeConnick-era ensemble (*Captain Marvel* vol. 7): Helen Cobb (decedent, complicated legacy — see Mentors below), Tracy Burke (decedent), and the cohort of women aviators who form the cultural and emotional substrate of the bar-and-hangar scenes. Continued ambient presence through subsequent runs.

**Dynamic.** Not friendship in the dyadic sense but *containing structure*. The Banshee bar is one of the few documented spaces where the subject *sits still*. She leans on the bar, she listens, she lets older women talk over her, she defers tactically to people with no powers and forty years on the throttle. This is the most regulated her nervous system gets outside of Kamala-adjacent and Jessica-adjacent settings.

**Why it works.** Aviator culture predates the powers and is therefore one of the few domains in which Carol's identity does not have to be *defended*. Among the Banshees she is simply a pilot. The role-mediation makes intimacy survivable.

**Trust / safety.** Moderate-high, but mediated. She does not bring her cosmic-scale griefs into the bar; she brings the body that is exhausted by them and lets it be tended.

**Failure mode.** Erosion by attrition. Tracy's death and Helen's death were costly; each Banshee loss subtracts from the containing structure, and the subject has limited capacity to rebuild this kind of mediated-intimate community from scratch.

**Leverage.** Indirect. Threats to the bar, the surviving Banshees, or the aviator culture itself will produce protective response. More importantly, the bar is the *recovery setting* — disrupting it disrupts her primary non-mission decompression vector.

---

## 7. HELEN COBB — THE MENTOR-AS-MIRROR

**Provenance.** DeConnick *Captain Marvel* vol. 7. Cobb was Carol's flight idol, a generation older, a woman who had bent the same airframes and broken the same ceilings; revealed posthumously as ambivalent and possessive of Carol's powers, attempting to seize them through time-travel.

**Dynamic and significance.** Helen is the most psychologically informative mentor in the file precisely because the mentorship was *complicated by Helen's envy*. She was the woman Carol wanted to become, and she wanted to be Carol. The arc gave the subject a controlled rehearsal of the question *what do I owe the women who came before me, and what do I owe myself?* and she answered it without flinching.

**Trust / safety (retrospective).** Permanently downgraded. The relationship informs Carol's current mentorship style — she is *deliberate* about not being possessive of Kamala's trajectory, and the deliberateness is Helen-derived.

**Failure mode (lesson absorbed).** That mentors can be envious; that idolization is a vulnerability; that the women you build yourself toward may not have built themselves for you.

**Leverage.** Posthumous; invocations of Helen produce reflective rather than reactive response.

---

## 8. MAR-VELL — THE GHOST-MENTOR

**Provenance.** Originating relationship (*Captain Marvel* vol. 1, 1968–1969); the Kree officer whose physiology she inherited and whose name she eventually took. Their actual on-page time was brief; the relationship as it functions in her psychology is largely posthumous.

**Dynamic.** Idealized predecessor. He did not live to be disappointing. The mantle-assumption in 2012 was simultaneously tribute, claim, and corrective — she took the name a man had carried, with the deliberate consent of those who loved him, and made it the name of a woman.

**Trust / safety.** Inapplicable in living terms; symbolically, total. He is the rare male authority figure in her file who did not betray, withhold, or assault, largely because he did not stay alive long enough to.

**Failure mode.** Survivor-guilt as discrete subsyndromal feature (§4). The name-carrying is a continuous low-grade act of penance.

**Leverage.** Any narrative that frames her assumption of his name as illegitimate (Kree-revanchist arguments; Skrull-political arguments) will produce defensive response but also *self-doubt*, which is rare in her — the doubt is the lever.

---

## 9. MARIA HILL — THE COLLEAGUE-IN-COMMAND

**Provenance.** SHIELD-era and Alpha-Flight-era operational partnership. Distinct from the other relationships in this file because the bond is functional rather than affectional.

**Dynamic.** Two women who have both burned through their welcome at the top of organizations they helped build. Mutual recognition without mutual disclosure. Carol does not socialize with Hill; she *deploys* with her, and the deployment chemistry is high.

**Trust / safety.** High operational, low personal. Hill is one of the few people who can give Carol an order in an institutional setting and have it received as collegial rather than father-coded.

**Failure mode.** The relationship has no slack. Without the institutional frame it would not exist; with the frame it works precisely because no one is asking anything else of it.

**Leverage.** Institutional; remove the institution and the relationship loses force.

---

## 10. THE AVENGERS COHORT (AGGREGATE) — THE FAMILY THAT APPLAUDED

**Provenance.** *Avengers* #200 is the founding wound of this relationship; every subsequent Avengers tenure operates on top of that scar. The team has been her primary professional home, her primary site of betrayal, her primary site of repair, and her primary site of overreach, in that order, repeatedly.

**Dynamic.** Carol's relationship to the Avengers-as-entity is the relationship the rest of her file orbits. They are the chosen family who *failed to see* (§3 Trauma Signature), and her decades-long re-engagement with the team is, at one level, a sustained corrective: she will be present, she will be unmissable, she will be in command if possible, she will *make them see*. The pro-registration vote, the Mighty Avengers tenure, the Ultimates leadership, the CWII faction — read these as a continuous attempt to occupy a position in the team from which she cannot again be overridden.

**Trust / safety.** Cohort-conditional. Particular Avengers (Drew, Rhodey, eventually Stark) cleared the bar individually. The team-as-team operates on probation that never fully expires.

**Failure mode.** Cyclical. Every several years a team event produces the felt-sense of being unseen or overridden; she withdraws, she escalates, she returns. The cycle is the most stable feature of her professional life.

**Leverage.** High but diffuse. Pressure on the team produces protective response; pressure *from within* the team produces the historically-most-dangerous decision patterns in the file.

---

## 11. AMERICA CHAVEZ, KATE BISHOP, AND THE YOUNGER ENSEMBLE — THE SECOND-RING MENTEES

**Provenance.** Variously: Ultimates (vol. 2) with Chavez; intermittent crossover and crisis-team mentorship with Bishop, Riri Williams, and the post-Kamala generation.

**Dynamic.** Differentiated from the Kamala bond by intensity, not kind. She is available, she is generous with airtime, she defends them in rooms they are not in, she does not over-parent. The America Chavez relationship in particular reads as *peer mentorship* — Chavez does not need parenting and Carol does not offer it.

**Trust / safety.** Asymmetric protective, lower intensity than Kamala. She would walk through fire for any of them; she would not necessarily expect them to walk through fire for her, and that asymmetry is the point.

**Failure mode.** Generalized — any of these mentees in CWII-shaped jeopardy will produce the preempt-protect-override reflex (§5). Distribution of mentee-load may, perversely, *reduce* per-relationship overreach risk by diffusing it; this is the most optimistic note in the file.

**Leverage.** Vector-rich. Each of these younger heroes is a potential pressure point of moderate intensity.

---

## SYNTHESIS — THE TOPOLOGY

Read as a system, the chosen-family map shows three layers:

- **Inner ring (Drew; the ghost of Rhodey).** Unmediated intimacy. She is herself here, including the parts she does not show anywhere else.
- **Mid ring (Kamala; Stark; Monica; the Banshees as ensemble).** Mediated by role, by mantle, by shared substrate, by ritual. She is *most of herself* here, with role-appropriate filtering.
- **Outer ring (Hill; the wider Avengers; second-ring mentees).** Mediated by institution or by mission. She is the operational version of herself, and the version is excellent.

The structural vulnerability is the inner ring's smallness — one living member. The structural strength is the mid ring's density and the deliberateness of her mentorship work, which is the single most stabilizing behavior in her current life. The leverage map for anyone attempting to move the subject — adversarial or benevolent — follows this topology inversely: the closer to the center, the smaller the input required and the larger and less predictable the output.

She has, finally, built the chosen family her father's house denied her. She has built it on a foundation she does not entirely trust. She tends it with the discipline of a woman who knows what she lost the last time she assumed people who loved her would see what was being done to her in the room.


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

A relational map of antagonism and intimacy in the subject's life, treated together because in her case the two categories share a porous border. Carol Danvers has, with striking consistency, loved people she has also fought, and fought people whose pull on her interior life is indistinguishable from the pull of a lover. The throughline: she gravitates toward relationships organized around *capability* — those who match her power, threaten it, or are positioned to override it. The result is a roster heavy with peers-turned-adversaries and adversaries-turned-permanent-furniture in her interior architecture.

Each entry maps: (i) history of contact; (ii) prevailing dynamic; (iii) longitudinal evolution; (iv) trust/safety calibration as she currently holds it; (v) characteristic failure mode of the bond; (vi) leverage, in both directions, accessible to either party in extremis.

---

## I. RIVALS — Peers Whose Existence Reframes Hers

### Anthony Edward Stark

**History.** Avengers co-tenure dating to her first tour in the late seventies. Friendship calcified during her Warbird-era alcoholism: Stark, himself in recovery, ran her intervention, then her Avengers-tribunal court-martial when she refused it. He carried the friendship across her bottom and into her sobriety; she let him. *Civil War* (2006–07) aligned them on registration; *Civil War II* (2016) detonated them across the predictive-justice fault line — she pro-preemption, he opposing, both stubborn enough to push it to physical confrontation that nearly killed him.

**Dynamic.** The most consequential peer rivalry of her adult life because it is the only one structured by mutual *recognition of the same wound*. Stark sees the alcoholic in her because he is the alcoholic in himself; she resents and depends on this sight in equal measure. Their conflicts read as sibling-coded: contested authority, contested moral framing of harm-prevention, contested ownership of the "responsible adult in the room" role that each, separately, has organized a personality around.

**Evolution.** Intervention era — he is the man who refused to look away while she drowned. Registration era — they are aligned and it feels, briefly, like the friendship has matured into doctrine. CWII — the doctrine becomes the wedge: he, the futurist, will not accept probability as cause; she, the soldier, will not accept inaction as innocence. Post-CWII — long, slow, incomplete repair. She has not retracted the underlying logic that justified hitting him; she has accepted that hitting him was the wrong outcome of that logic. He, characteristically, forgave faster than she has forgiven herself.

**Trust / Safety.** High in operational matters; she trusts his engineering, his tactical read, and — critically — his discretion about her drinking history. Low in matters where his judgment supersedes hers; she experiences his correction as paternal in the worst sense.

**Failure mode.** Mutual conviction-cascade. When both lock onto incompatible frames, neither stands down; the friendship cannot generate a third-party arbiter either will accept.

**Leverage.** *He on her:* the only living witness, besides Rhodes, who has seen her impaired and chosen not to weaponize it; the implicit threat is therefore not exposure but withdrawal of that mercy. *She on him:* she knows the futurist's blind spot — the inability to credit anyone else's predictive model as legitimate — and can name it in a register he cannot dismiss as ignorance.

### Rogue (Anna Marie)

**History.** *Avengers Annual* #10 (1981). Then-villain Rogue absorbed her powers, memories, and — by Claremont's framing — a substantive portion of her self, permanently. Carol awoke a blank; Rogue carried her in her head as an intrusive second consciousness for years. The two have orbited each other across decades: hostile, then uneasy-coexistent in X-Men-Avengers crossovers, never reconciled in the way fan narrative sometimes implies.

**Dynamic.** The single most somatically intimate adversary in her file. Rogue did not kill her; Rogue *wore* her. The injury has no clean clinical analog and no clean interpersonal one. Their interactions carry the charge of an assault survivor encountering the assailant after the assailant has, herself, become a functioning person — the moral arithmetic does not resolve.

**Evolution.** Early: pure enmity, with Carol's depowered absence functioning as proof of harm. Middle: Rogue's rehabilitation into the X-Men creates an etiquette problem the larger hero community resolves by simply not asking Carol about it. Late: working proximity in events forces functional civility; the work is not friendship, it is professional containment of an unhealed wound.

**Trust / Safety.** Operationally minimal; personally zero. She will fight beside Rogue and would not, under foreseeable circumstances, accept a debrief alone with her.

**Failure mode.** Re-traumatization on contact she did not control the framing of. Any forced intimacy — therapy session, mission requiring touch, attempt at apology — risks reactivating the original violation rather than resolving it.

**Leverage.** *Rogue on her:* possesses, or possessed, the literal contents of her memory, including memories she does not herself have access to post-absorption. This is a leverage no one else in her life holds and Carol manages it by sealing the topic. *She on Rogue:* the moral standing of the wronged, exercised with discipline; she has never weaponized it, which is itself a form of held power.

### Moonstone (Karla Sofen)

**History.** Original Ms. Marvel-era antagonist; psychiatrist-turned-power-thief who took the Moonstone gem and built a career arc partly defined by attempted appropriation of Carol's role. Recurring across Thunderbolts and Dark Avengers eras, including impersonation periods that have shadowed Carol's reputation.

**Dynamic.** The dark mirror. Sofen is what Carol would be if the trauma had metabolized into exploitation rather than service: the same hunger for capability, the same comfort with command, none of the ethical brake. Carol reads her with unusual accuracy because the diagnostic acumen runs the wrong way too — Sofen, trained, sees Carol's defenses with professional clarity and uses them.

**Trust / Safety.** Adversarial baseline assumed permanent. Of all her rogues, this is the one whose verbal contact she most needs to keep brief; Sofen talks to the substrate, not the uniform.

**Failure mode.** Engagement on Sofen's terms — psychological rather than physical. Carol's best response is closure-of-distance and termination of dialogue; when she lingers in conversation, Sofen scores.

**Leverage.** *Sofen on her:* clinical-grade access to the alcoholism / dissociation / father-injury complex, delivered as needle rather than diagnosis. *She on Sofen:* raw physical overmatch and the moral weight of having actually earned the title Sofen wants.

### Mystique (Raven Darkhölme)

**History.** Brotherhood-era handler of the Rogue who absorbed her. Carol has held Mystique culpable for the original violation by proximity — Rogue as protégée, Mystique as architect — and the file includes a documented period in which Carol pursued Mystique with intent to kill (*Ms. Marvel* vol. 2, Reed run, post-*House of M*).

**Dynamic.** The displaced object. Rogue is unkillable in Carol's moral frame because Rogue has become a hero; Mystique is the residue onto whom the surviving rage attaches. Carol knows this about herself; she pursues anyway. This is the clearest published instance of her stress-ladder reaching the rung where she becomes the person she does not want to be.

**Trust / Safety.** None and irrelevant. Mystique is treated as a recurring threat-vector with personal weight.

**Failure mode.** Loss of professional remove. With Mystique specifically, Carol's interrogation-discipline and minimum-force standards have, on record, failed; the encounter pulls her toward an executioner's posture she otherwise refuses.

**Leverage.** *Mystique on her:* knowledge that she can reliably destabilize Carol by surfacing the Rogue topic obliquely. *She on Mystique:* the raw fact that she is one of a small number of people on Earth who can win the fight outright.

### Yon-Rogg

**History.** The Kree commander whose original engagement with Mar-Vell catalyzed the Psyche-Magnitron explosion that powered her. Recurring antagonist across Kree-arc stories; positioned, sometimes explicitly, as the proximal cause of her transformation.

**Dynamic.** Adversary-as-origin. He is the figure her power-history can be traced through, which makes him the closest thing in her file to a person she cannot defeat by killing, because killing him removes nothing she has not already integrated. Their encounters carry a fated quality she resents.

**Trust / Safety.** Zero, unwavering.

**Failure mode.** The temptation of monocausal explanation. Yon-Rogg flatters the part of her that wants her transformation to have a single villain; she has to refuse the gift each time.

**Leverage.** *He on her:* narrative ownership of the origin — he can frame her existence as his accident. *She on him:* sustained physical superiority and the political fact that she now outranks the institution he served.

### Vox Supreme / the post-Empyre Kree-Skrull command structures

**History.** Late-period antagonists from the Stohl and post-*Empyre* runs, weaponizing Kree biotech against her hybrid physiology specifically.

**Dynamic.** Institutional adversary. Carol's quarrel here is with hierarchy rather than individual; the Kree command is the father-coded authority structure at galactic scale, repeatedly telling her to stand down on grounds of her own biology. She refuses by reflex.

**Trust / Safety.** Hostile-institutional baseline.

**Failure mode.** Escalation. Institutions she reads as father-coded receive her maximum disproportionate response.

**Leverage.** *They on her:* genetic-level access — biotech tailored to her hybrid structure constitutes a category of weapon no other adversary deploys. *She on them:* the symbolic weight of a hybrid who took their war-name and made it human-coded.

---

## II. ENEMIES — Those Without Reconciliation

### Mystique-of-Avengers-#200 / Marcus Immortus

**History.** *Avengers* #200 (1980). Son of Immortus. Abducted Carol to Limbo, subjected her to what the issue framed as courtship and what *Avengers Annual* #10 corrected to rape: prolonged psychological manipulation under temporal duress, forced impregnation, accelerated gestation, parturition within days, then return to Earth-time with a child who was the perpetrator. The Avengers congratulated the union.

**Dynamic.** No relationship in her file is more determinative and there is no living counterparty to relate *to*; Marcus aged out of existence during the return trip. The enemy here is functionally the event, which is why this entry properly belongs in this section rather than in the medical file alone: the relational injury is to the Avengers as much as to Marcus.

**Evolution.** The enemy persists as a template. Every subsequent encounter in which her bodily sovereignty is questioned, overridden, or framed as consent-when-it-was-not activates Marcus-coded response: disproportionate, immediate, unappealable.

**Trust / Safety.** Inapplicable to Marcus; partially restored, eventually, with the Avengers, but the original cohort that applauded has never been forgiven as a body — only as individuals, one by one, slowly.

**Failure mode.** The injury is the failure mode. Anything in its echo register collapses her capacity for graduated response.

**Leverage.** *The event on her:* permanent. *She on it:* the long discipline of having named it, of having let Claremont's correction stand as canonical record, of mentoring Kamala in part to ensure no younger woman will be left unseen by her chosen family in the way she was.

### The Brood

**History.** *Uncanny X-Men* #161–#167. Captured, implanted, subjected to prolonged biological violation that catalyzed the Binary transformation. The original captivity is the second great bodily-sovereignty injury of her life, following Marcus by one publication year.

**Dynamic.** Species-level enemy. The Brood are not characters to her; they are a category of insult to which she responds with categorical violence. This is one of the few engagements where her minimum-force discipline is consciously suspended in advance.

**Trust / Safety.** Categorical hostility.

**Failure mode.** Pre-emption, openly. She has stated, on panel and across runs, that she will not wait to see what a given Brood encounter intends.

**Leverage.** *Them on her:* somatic memory of implantation, accessible by environmental cues — chitinous architecture, certain biotech smells in-narrative. *She on them:* Binary-tier power, which is to say more than they can survive.

### Ulysses Cain (operational, not personal)

**History.** Inhuman precognitive whose visions she relied on through *Civil War II*. Not an enemy in the conventional sense; the catalyst of her largest published moral failure.

**Dynamic.** Instrument that became indictment. Ulysses is, in her interior accounting, the figure who proved that her instinct toward preemption — when armed with what looked like certainty — produced the wrong outcomes. He is filed under enemy because his continued existence is a continued referendum on her judgment.

**Trust / Safety.** Working civility; deep avoidance.

**Failure mode.** Re-engagement of the predictive-justice frame. She will not work with precognitive intelligence again on his model, and she watches herself for the temptation.

**Leverage.** *He on her:* none deliberate; the existence of his record is the leverage. *She on him:* she has, characteristically, not blamed him publicly, absorbing the failure as command-level rather than asset-level. This is its own kind of held power.

### Vulture / Sabretooth / generic recurring brawlers

**History.** Long catalog of physical antagonists whom she defeats without permanent interpersonal weight.

**Dynamic.** Operational, not relational. Filed for completeness; they do not shape her.

**Trust / Safety.** N/A.

**Failure mode.** None of note.

**Leverage.** None of note in either direction.

---

## III. LOVERS AND INTIMATES — The Short, Charged List

### James "Rhodey" Rhodes

**History.** Air Force adjacent professional acquaintance for years before the relationship; intimate partnership formalized in the DeConnick run (2012–) and developed across the lead-up to *Civil War II*, where his death in the opening pages constitutes the inciting trauma of her overreach. Pre-existing context of mutual respect between two career-military pilots of color and gender in institutions not built for them; the relationship rested on shared service-frame.

**Dynamic.** The healthiest sustained romantic bond in her file. Rhodey, uniquely, was a partner who matched her on the three axes where she most needed match: aviator culture, command experience, and the lived knowledge that the body in the cockpit is the instrument and the asset both. He did not require her to translate herself. He also — critically — did not flinch from her capability, which had been the silent disqualifier in most of her prior romantic attempts.

**Evolution.** Slow professional-to-personal migration; brief, dense intimate window; abrupt loss. The relationship was never given the years it would have needed to test her under domestic ambiguity, which is the register where her romantic life has historically failed. We cannot know whether they would have survived ordinary time; we know they did not get the chance.

**Trust / Safety.** Within the bond, near-total — the highest reading in her file. Post-loss, the trust did not transfer; it scarred over.

**Failure mode.** The bond ended by death, not failure, but the *survivor pattern* is failure-shaped: grief was metabolized as command intensification, not mourning. The CWII detentions are, in part, the form her unmourned grief took.

**Leverage.** Posthumous and absolute. Any framing of duty, sacrifice, or prevention-of-harm that invokes Rhodey will move her in directions she cannot independently audit. Adversaries with intelligence on this fact have a key to her judgment.

### Michael Rossi

**History.** Air Force intelligence colleague from her pre-powered era; intermittent intimate across early *Ms. Marvel* and later. Among the earliest documented partners.

**Dynamic.** Pre-transformation template.
