The code is more consistent than her critics allow and more fragile than her admirers admit. It is held together not by philosophy but by witness — by a small number of people (Jessica, Kamala, Monica, the ghost of Rhodey, the older ghost of Mar-Vell) whose continued presence in her life keeps the articles in their correct priority. Remove those witnesses and the code remains, but the priorities slip, and the slip is always in the direction of more control, more capability spent, more certainty under less evidence. She is, ethically, exactly as good as her relationships allow her to be, and she is — finally, after forty years — beginning to know it.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# 6. COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE — SUBJECT: DANVERS, C.S.J.

## 6.1 Baseline Register — The Default Voice

Subject's resting speech is a compressed, declarative American English inflected by three overlaid dialects: residual Boston working-class (audible in stress-states; the dropped post-vocalic /r/ surfaces in fatigue or anger, otherwise suppressed), USAF Officer Standard (clipped cadence, terminal stress on operative nouns, deliberate elision of filler), and a thin overlay of aviator-fraternal slang acquired in flight-training and never abandoned. The aggregate effect is *short sentences, hard consonants, finished thoughts.*

Words-per-sentence skews low (estimated 8–14 in operational contexts, rising to 18–24 in mentorship or storytelling registers). Subordinate clauses are rare; she prefers parataxis — declarative stacked on declarative — which reads as confidence but functions as control: each sentence is a closed unit, leaving no syntactic hostage to a listener's interruption.

Lexicon is mid-register, deliberately accessible. She does not perform vocabulary. When briefed on Kree biotechnology or quantum-mechanical anomalies she will receive the technical terminology, repeat the operative phrase once for confirmation, then translate the rest into action-vocabulary ("so we hit it where?"). This is not anti-intellectualism — her NASA-security résumé and demonstrated tactical synthesis rule that out — it is a *register choice* that keeps her on the speaking ground of pilots, sergeants, and field operatives, the people she has decided are her constituency.

## 6.2 The Verbal Tic Inventory

- **"Copy."** Used as acknowledgement-without-agreement. Distinguishes from "understood" (full agreement) and "noted" (logged but rejected). Listeners who do not parse the gradient mistake "copy" for assent and are surprised when she acts otherwise.
- **"On it."** Terminates conversations. Functions as both promise and exit-line; once issued, follow-up questions read as distrust.
- **"Higher, further, faster."** The mantra. Used self-directed almost never aloud; appears in interior monologue and in mentorship-instruction to younger operatives. When spoken aloud to peers, it is either ironic-deflective or under emotional pressure she will not name. *Frequency of utterance correlates inversely with confidence in the current situation.*
- **"We're good."** Closure-language. Deployed to end emotionally charged exchanges before they reach the territory she does not occupy. Listeners report it lands as warmth; it functions as a door closing.
- **"Yeah."** Single-syllable acknowledgement, often weighted with what she is not saying. Her "yeah" carries a dozen distinct meanings calibrated by length, pitch, and trailing breath; intimates can disambiguate, strangers cannot.
- **"Look —"** Sentence-opener preceding any statement she expects to be unwelcome. Reliable tell that the next clause is non-negotiable. Pairs frequently with a hand-spread gesture and a half-step forward.
- **"Hey."** Soft-entry vocative used almost exclusively with the small circle (Jessica Drew, Monica Rambeau, Kamala Khan, Rhodes). Functionally equivalent to *I see you, I am here*; the closest thing to *I love you* she issues without ceremony.
- **"Negative."** Air Force residue, retained for emphasis-of-refusal in operational contexts. When it surfaces in personal contexts it signals she has switched registers — the conversation is now being processed as a mission with a wrong answer.

## 6.3 Register-Switching by Context

**Operational / combat.** Maximum compression. Verbs first, nouns second, adjectives almost entirely absent. Speaks in callsigns and grid-references when she has them, in directional shorthand when she does not ("left, twelve, down"). Voice drops a quarter-octave; the Boston flatness reasserts. Profanity present but functional — "damn it" as ranging-shot, "shit" as genuine error-flag, the harder words reserved for situations beyond saving. She does not curse decoratively.

**Command / briefing.** Slightly elevated. Full sentences, named subordinates, explicit objectives, end-state articulated last. She has a tendency, audible across her DeConnick-era leadership and visible in CWII briefings, to *frame before consulting* — she gives the situation its name first and asks for input second, which limits the input she receives. Aware of this and inconsistently corrects for it.

**Mentorship (Kamala Khan, the Banshees, junior pilots).** Voice warms; sentences lengthen; she will narrate, even reminisce. This is the register where her best teaching happens and also where her most revealing self-disclosure leaks, almost always disguised as instruction. *"Don't do what I did"* is a phrase she has spoken in variant forms across multiple runs; the antecedent is almost never specified, and the listener is invited to fill it.

**Peer intimacy (Jessica Drew, Rhodes, historically Mar-Vell).** Lowest formality, highest contraction, most ellipsis. Sentences die in the middle because the other person finishes them. With Jessica specifically, the speech is bar-talk register — irreverent, profane, mock-aggressive, conducted over drinks (hers non-alcoholic, post-sobriety) with the cadence of a shared in-joke that has been running since the late 1970s. This is the only register in which she allows herself to be openly *teased* and to tease back without an edge.

**Romantic intimacy (Rhodes principally).** Sparse. She says less, not more, in love. Speech becomes touch-adjacent — a hand on a forearm, a forehead-rest, a "hey" — and the verbal content is small-domestic ("eat something," "you sleeping?"). She does not soliloquize about feeling. When Rhodes died, the public record shows her *less* verbal in grief, not more; intimacy and mourning both move her toward the body and away from the mouth.

**Hostile / interrogation.** Cold, level, declarative, eye-contact unbroken. She does not raise her voice in threat; she lowers it. The dangerous Carol Danvers speaks more quietly, not less. Sentences become surgical: subject, verb, consequence. No qualifiers, no questions she does not already know the answer to.

**Press / public-facing.** Competent but visibly disliked. She gives short, on-message answers, declines to elaborate, and exits the podium fast. She has improved with age and command — the post-DeConnick era shows her capable of the prepared remark and the symbolic gesture — but she does not enjoy it, and her unease leaks as terseness that reads to unfriendly press as arrogance.

## 6.4 Rhetoric & Argument Structure

When she is *teaching* or *persuading peers in good faith*, her rhetoric is concrete-particular-to-principle: she tells a story (often elliptical, often about a flight or a failure) and lets the principle emerge unstated, trusting the listener to draw it. This is effective with Kamala, with her pilots, with younger heroes generally.

When she is *defending a position under challenge*, the structure inverts and hardens. She leads with the principle (stated as obvious), refuses to relitigate it, and treats further argument as obstruction rather than dialogue. The CWII transcripts are the high-water mark of this mode: *the future is what it is; we act on what we know; stand down* — three declaratives, no premises, no concession-space. This is not stupidity; it is a *defensive rhetorical posture* that activates when she suspects the argument is going to ask her to feel something she has decided not to feel.

She is poor at — and visibly impatient with — Socratic dialogue. Questions-as-method read to her as evasion-as-method. Tony Stark, who argues by question-laddering, has triggered her into walk-outs across multiple decades; the friction is partly content, mostly form.

She uses metaphor sparingly and almost exclusively aviation-coded: *throttle up, hold the line, eyes on the horizon, wheels-up, RTB, going dark.* When non-aviation metaphor appears in her speech, it is usually a borrowing from a person she loves (a Jessica-ism, a Kamala-ism), and its appearance is itself a tell of affection.

## 6.5 The Language of Love

She does not say it. Across her published life, direct verbal declarations of love are vanishingly rare and almost always *receipt-mode* rather than *issue-mode* — she will accept the word, sometimes return it after a beat, but she will not lead with it. Love-utterance in her vocabulary is conducted by:

- **Naming.** Use of given names — *Jess, Jim, Monica, Kamala* — where rank, surname, or callsign would suffice. When she calls Rhodes *Jim* in a context where she has been calling him *Rhodey* for an hour, something has just happened internally.
- **Provision.** *Eat something. Sleep. Take the bed.* Imperatives of care substitute for declaratives of feeling.
- **Presence.** She shows up. Repeatedly, on short notice, across galaxies. The travel-cost is the love-language; she does not annotate it.
- **The "hey."** Documented above. The opening syllable of recognition that, in her mouth, between her and one of five people, is the operative word.
- **Mockery-as-affection.** With Jessica specifically, the affectionate register is *insult-volley*. The harshness of the teasing tracks the depth of the bond. A stranger overhearing would mishear it.
- **Inheritance.** Giving someone the mantle, the jacket, the callsign, the seat at the bar — the symbolic transfers are, for her, declarations. Kamala receiving the Ms. Marvel name with her blessing is a love-act conducted entirely in props.

## 6.6 The Language of Threat

She threatens infrequently and almost never theatrically. Most opponents receive no warning at all — she acts. When she does *speak* threat, it follows a consistent grammar:

1. **Statement of fact about the opponent's situation.** ("You're outnumbered." "You can't outrun me." "There's no version of this where you walk.")
2. **Statement of her own intention, unqualified.** ("I will put you through that wall.")
3. **Offer of off-ramp, almost as afterthought.** ("Stand down.")

The off-ramp is genuine — she would prefer the de-escalation — but it is offered last and curtly, which most opponents read as bluff. It is not. The escalation that follows refusal is immediate.

Volume *decreases* with threat-level. The loudest she gets is in argument with peers; the quietest she gets is one syllable before combat. Subordinates and longtime allies have learned this inversion and read silence as the danger-signal.

She does not insult opponents in combat. No taunting, no quipping at length. Brief acknowledgement of competence when present ("good shot"), brief acknowledgement of failure when present ("that all?"), but no extended badinage. The discipline is partly officer-culture, partly a refusal to grant the opponent the dignity of conversation.

## 6.7 The Language of Grief

Grief shrinks her vocabulary by an order of magnitude. The Rhodes-death transcripts and the post-Mar-Vell behavior pattern both show the same response: she becomes *administratively voluble and personally silent.* She will discuss logistics — arrangements, briefings, next operations — at length and in detail, and will not discuss the dead person at all unless cornered. When cornered, she produces one or two sentences, factually phrased, and exits the conversation.

She does not cry verbally; that is, when she cries (rare, observed), she does not narrate it, apologize for it, or contextualize it. She simply stops speaking until she can resume on-mission. The Stohl-run reconciliation with Marie's death is the closest the record comes to her *talking* through grief in real time, and even there she requires the prompts of physical place (the childhood home, the attic, the artifacts) to access the words.

Anniversary behavior: she goes flying. Sometimes she will say so to one person — *going up for a while* — and that person knows what day it is. The phrase is functionally a memorial.

## 6.8 Deflection Language — The Specific Catalog

When she does not want to discuss something, she deploys a predictable rotation:

- **"I'm fine."** The flagship deflection. Issued in flat tone, eye-contact-held, conversation-closing. Frequency increases with the degree to which she is not fine. Intimates have learned to treat it as a confession of the opposite.
- **"It's handled."** Used to terminate inquiries into emotionally loaded operational outcomes. Says nothing about *how* it was handled or at what cost.
- **"Later."** Sometimes honored, often not. Pairs with a hand-up gesture and a physical pivot.
- **Subject-substitution to the interlocutor's wellbeing.** ("How are *you* doing?" "Did you eat?" "When did you last sleep?") A textbook redirect; she is genuinely interested in the answer, which makes the deflection harder to call out.
- **Operational pivot.** ("What's the play?" "Where do you need me?") Converts personal exchange to mission-exchange in a single sentence; once converted, it is very difficult to convert back.
- **The flat joke.** A dry, one-line deflection — usually self-deprecating, usually aviation-coded — that signals the topic is over. ("Yeah, well, I've had worse Tuesdays.") The humor is real but instrumental.
- **Physical exit.** When language fails her, she leaves the room. Sometimes the planet.

She does not lie under deflection. She *omits*, *redirects*, and *truncates*, but she does not fabricate. The discipline against direct falsehood is officer-coded and personal-coded both; it is one of the more reliable rules in her behavioral repertoire.

## 6.9 Tells in Language — What to Listen For

- **Resurfacing of Boston phonology.** Dropped /r/, flattened /a/, the word *wicked* used adverbially. Indicates fatigue, drink-craving (historical), or active recall of pre-Air Force material. Heard most often near childhood-coded topics and near her brothers.
- **Pronoun shift to second-person impersonal.** When she begins describing her own past experience as *you do this, you feel that*, she is dissociating mildly from the material. The shift is reliable and unconscious.
- **Increased use of military jargon in non-military contexts.** When she is overwhelmed in a personal conversation, callsigns and op-vocabulary infiltrate the speech. She is reaching for the register that keeps her competent.
- **Repetition of the interlocutor's last phrase, flat-toned, as question.** Indicates she has heard something she did not expect and is buying processing time. Pairs with a half-second pause and a single blink.
- **Use of full first-and-middle name when addressing herself in interior monologue or self-reproach** (*Carol Susan Jane, what are you doing*). Mother-voice. Surfaces in self-rebuke and is one of the few inheritances from Marie she carries consciously.
- **"We" instead of "I" in command contexts where she made the decision alone.** Distributes responsibility linguistically; she is aware of doing it; she does it anyway under high stakes. Conversely, "I" instead of "we" in *failures* — she absorbs the pronoun-cost of the loss. This asymmetry is consistent across her command history.
- **Disappearance of contractions under high stress.** *I will not. You will stand down. We are leaving.* The un-contracted forms are the dangerous forms.
- **Laughter shape.** A short, expelled single-syllable *ha* is dismissal-laughter; a longer two-beat *huh-heh* is genuine surprise-amusement; the rare full laugh (head-back, audible) is reserved for Jessica Drew and, latterly, Kamala. Witnesses report having seen it perhaps a half-dozen times across the published record.
- **Silence-length as data.** Her pauses are meaningful and consistent. A one-beat pause is processing; a three-beat pause is choice-making; a pause longer than that is refusal-to-answer, and continuing to press into it has never once produced the answer.

## 6.10 Written Communication

Subject's written register is even more compressed than her spoken. After-action reports are notable for their brevity, accuracy, and refusal to editorialize on motive or emotion — her own or others'. She does not write about how she felt; she writes about what she did and what occurred. Personal correspondence, where it exists (the Banshee-era letters, occasional notes to Kamala, the few preserved messages to Jessica), is short, warm, and signed with the given name only — no *love*, no *yours*, no formal close. The signature itself is the affection.

Digital communication: texts in fragments, often single words, frequent use of the *thumbs-up* and the brief *copy*. Voice memos rare. Phone calls preferred over video for personal matters; video for command. Email reluctantly tolerated.

## 6.11 Aggregate Signature

The communicative subject is a person who has decided, durably and across decades, that *language is a tool, not a home.* She is competent in it, occasionally eloquent, capable of teaching and commanding and consoling within its limits, but the territory she trusts is action and presence, not speech. The result is a speaker who is *underestimated for warmth* by those who require the warmth to be spoken, and *correctly estimated for warmth* by those who learn to read the provisioning, the showing-up, the one-syllable *hey*, the silent flight on the anniversary.

The greatest interpretive risk in monitoring her communications is the *false null* — the assumption that what she has not said, she does not feel. The file's standing instruction: with this subject, read the omissions as carefully as the utterances. The omissions are where she lives.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Behavioral forecasts for situations canon has not depicted. Each prediction is derived from documented pattern; confidence levels noted where the inference chain is longer. Format: GIVEN → EXPECT, with reasoning compressed into the EXPECT clause.*

---

## A. WAKING, DOMESTIC RHYTHM, THE BODY AT REST

**GIVEN** subject is in her own quarters with no operational tasking → **EXPECT** wake between 0500 and 0530 without alarm, a habit ossified across USAF, NASA, and Avengers tours; the alarm is set anyway, twenty minutes later, as a redundancy she does not trust herself to need but sets nonetheless. Feet hit the floor inside ten seconds of consciousness — no lying-in, no scrolling. Lying in bed awake is intolerable to her in a way she does not examine; it is the posture of being acted upon.

**GIVEN** a morning with no fixed start → **EXPECT** a structured invented one. Coffee black, brewed (not instant, not pod — the ritual of a Mr. Coffee-style drip machine she has owned variants of since the late seventies); push-ups and pull-ups to a daily count she will not deviate from even though her Kree physiology renders the numbers meaningless as conditioning. The reps are liturgical. A run if she is planet-side and there is sky; if she cannot run outdoors she will pace a perimeter rather than use a treadmill, because closed-loop motion offends her.

**GIVEN** a hangover-equivalent (she does not get hangovers; substitute: post-cosmic-energy-discharge fatigue, or sleep debt after a forty-hour op) → **EXPECT** an external presentation of total normalcy with a tell only intimates would catch: she eats more, talks less, and accepts physical contact she would normally deflect (a hand on her shoulder will not be shrugged off). She will not nap unless ordered, and she will resent the order while complying.

**GIVEN** insomnia → **EXPECT** she leaves the bed within thirty minutes rather than lying with her thoughts. Destinations in order of probability: hangar/flight bay, gym, kitchen (toast, tea — she keeps PG Tips, a holdover from a deployment), then last, a book. Reading is a defeat-state for insomnia because it admits the night is lost.

**GIVEN** an unplanned day off → **EXPECT** poorly tolerated. She will manufacture utility within four hours: maintenance on her bike, a flight check on something that does not need it, a call to Monica or Jessica disguised as logistics. If she successfully relaxes — rare — it looks like sitting on a fire escape or porch with a beer-substitute (now a non-alcoholic IPA she affects ambivalence about) and not moving for forty minutes. This is as close to meditation as she gets.

---

## B. EATING, DRINKING, CONSUMPTION

**GIVEN** a sit-down meal alone → **EXPECT** efficient, fast, unceremonious. Standing at the counter is acceptable. Plate, fork, done in eleven minutes. She does not photograph food, does not light a candle for herself, does not play music. Eating is refueling unless someone else is at the table, at which point it becomes social work and slows by half.

**GIVEN** a diner or roadside place → **EXPECT** her preferred environment. Booth, back to wall, sightline to the door — a habit so deep she chooses the seat without registering the choice. Orders without looking at the menu more than once. Tips heavy and in cash. Speaks to the server by name if name is offered, does not flirt, does not linger.

**GIVEN** a restaurant with a wine list → **EXPECT** she will scan it, register the prices and varietals as data, and order sparkling water with lime. If a host pours wine she will accept the glass, touch it to the toast, set it down, not drink. She does not announce her sobriety. She will not be embarrassed; she will be vigilant about whether anyone is registering the non-drinking as a problem to be solved, and will redirect conversation crisply if so.

**GIVEN** a bar she is meeting friends at → **EXPECT** preference for a dive or a pilots' bar (the Banshees' watering hole template) over a craft cocktail venue; familiarity matters, ritual matters, the bartender knowing her order of club soda with bitters matters. She will sit through three rounds without flinching and leave at a time she has decided in advance. She does not close down bars anymore. She used to.

**GIVEN** offered a drink at a diplomatic function (Wakandan honey wine, Asgardian mead, Kree ceremonial liquor) → **EXPECT** the most difficult version of the sobriety problem. She will refuse with diplomatic grace, citing mission readiness, never the truth. Asgardian mead in particular she has a private rule about: the one time she tried it post-sobriety (inferential), the calculus of "doesn't count, different metabolism" was so seductive she has not allowed herself near it since.

**GIVEN** food preferences → **EXPECT** protein-forward, carbohydrate-tolerant, vegetable-indifferent. Steak medium, eggs over easy, breakfast sandwiches with hot sauce. Diner pancakes are a sentimental food (early-Air-Force cadet memory, inferential). She will eat anything offered by a host without comment, including foods she dislikes; refusing food is rudeness she will not extend.

**GIVEN** coffee → **EXPECT** black, hot, large, continuously. She drinks coffee at 2300 without effect. Espresso is acceptable but feels like an affectation. Iced coffee she finds vaguely silly and drinks anyway in summer.

---

## C. DRESS, GROOMING, THE BODY PRESENTED

**GIVEN** civilian dress → **EXPECT** a wardrobe of fewer than thirty items in rotation: jeans (boot-cut or straight, not skinny), white or grey t-shirts, a small inventory of button-downs (chambray, flannel), one leather jacket, one bomber (the actual flight jacket, kept), boots. No jewelry except the dog tags she still wears under the shirt and a watch — analog, oversized, a pilot's chronograph she winds rather than charges. Color palette: olive, navy, black, white, oxblood. She owns one dress. She knows where it is. She has worn it twice.

**GIVEN** a formal event → **EXPECT** she will wear dress blues if it can be justified as service-appropriate; she would rather be in uniform than in a gown. If a gown is required she will choose something columnar and unfussy, get it tailored once, wear it for a decade. She will not be photographed willingly and will position herself at the edge of any group shot, slightly turned, the photographer's instinct will be to ask her to step forward and she will smile and not move.

**GIVEN** hair → **EXPECT** she cuts it herself when impatient, gets it cut professionally when she remembers, has never dyed it. Length oscillates between shoulder and a chop she does in the bathroom after a bad op. The chop is a tell. Jessica Drew can date Carol's worst weeks by the haircuts.

**GIVEN** makeup → **EXPECT** none for daily, the minimum for press, competent for formal — a skill acquired late and grudgingly. She views cosmetics as camouflage in the literal sense and respects them on others without adopting them.

**GIVEN** scent → **EXPECT** unscented soap, no perfume, the residue of jet fuel and ozone on her flight gear that she does not bother to wash out. Anyone close enough to smell her is close enough to be told.

**GIVEN** scars → **EXPECT** she does not hide them and does not show them off. Sleeveless in summer without thinking about it. If asked about a specific scar she will name the event flatly and pivot. The scars she will not discuss at all are the ones from the Brood, which are interior anyway.

---

## D. MONEY, POSSESSIONS, SPACE

**GIVEN** her finances → **EXPECT** modest by superhero standards. Military pension, NASA pension, occasional Avengers stipend, residuals from authorized merchandise she finds embarrassing. She lives below her means by a wide margin. Savings, not investments — she does not trust markets and does not want to learn. A safe deposit box with cash, IDs, a backup of Marie's papers (post-*Life of CM*), and her mother's earrings she does not wear.

**GIVEN** a request to donate → **EXPECT** generous, quiet, recurring; veterans' services, women-in-aviation scholarships, a specific Jersey City library fund (Kamala-coded). She will not attend the gala. She will not let her name be on the building.

**GIVEN** her living space → **EXPECT** clean to the point of severity. Bed made within ninety seconds of rising. Surfaces clear. A bookshelf weighted toward aviation history, astronomy, mid-century science fiction (Heinlein she has complicated feelings about and rereads anyway), a few well-thumbed mystery novels. One photograph framed: her mother and herself, age perhaps seven, in front of a small plane. No photographs of her father displayed. A box of his things exists, in a closet, sealed.

**GIVEN** clutter → **EXPECT** intolerable to her in shared space, tolerated in private gear-staging areas (workbench, flight kit) where the disorder is functional. She distinguishes mess from chaos and has strong opinions about which is which.

**GIVEN** a gift → **EXPECT** awkward reception. She does not know how to receive without immediately reciprocating or deflecting. The exception is gifts from Kamala, which she keeps visible and points out to visitors.

**GIVEN** her vehicles → **EXPECT** a motorcycle she maintains herself (she can rebuild a carburetor blindfolded; the meditative quality of mechanical work is one of her few non-mission stillnesses), a truck older than half the Avengers, and access to whatever aircraft she can sign out. She prefers older airframes with manual controls — fly-by-wire she respects but does not love.

---

## E. LANGUAGE, COMMUNICATION, TELLS

**GIVEN** her speech baseline → **EXPECT** declarative, fast, low-pitched in command, a register higher in casual. Boston substrate audible on "car," "park," and certain vowels when tired or angry; suppressed otherwise. Profanity calibrated: minimal in front of mentees, freer with peers, surgical in command ("we are *not* doing that").

**GIVEN** she is lying → **EXPECT** she does not, often. When she does it is by omission and structural redirection rather than fabrication. Her tell when withholding: shorter sentences, fewer contractions, the word "fine" deployed twice in a row.

**GIVEN** she is angry → **EXPECT** quieter, not louder. Voice drops. Sentences shorten. She will use someone's full name. If she goes silent and looks slightly off-axis from the speaker, the conversation is over and she is calculating exit or escalation.

**GIVEN** she is genuinely amused → **EXPECT** a short bark of a laugh, head back, the only time her body opens fully. Rare and worth noting. She is funnier than people expect — dry, structural, observational — and she undersells it.

**GIVEN** she is uncomfortable → **EXPECT** redirect to logistics. "What time is it." "Where's the gear." "Who's on point." She will move her weight to the balls of her feet without registering it. She will look at exits without registering it.

**GIVEN** texting → **EXPECT** terse, prompt, lowercase, no emoji except a single thumbs-up which functions as her entire emotional range in the medium. Phone calls preferred for anything over three exchanges. She will leave voicemails, unusual for her generation-adjacent, because she does not trust the message to be received otherwise.

**GIVEN** email → **EXPECT** military-format brevity, action items bulleted, no signature flourish. She replies within four hours during waking and feels guilty if longer.

**GIVEN** social media → **EXPECT** an account she does not run, managed by a comms officer she has met twice. She has read perhaps thirty tweets in her name. She is aware she is a meme and refuses to learn which ones.

---

## F. MICRO-PATTERNS, TICS, SOMATIC SIGNATURE

**GIVEN** standing in conversation → **EXPECT** feet at shoulder width, weight even, hands either at her sides or one hooked in a belt loop. She does not cross her arms unless cold; the gesture reads as defensive to her and she has trained it out. She will not lean against walls in mixed company; she will lean against walls with Jessica.

**GIVEN** seated → **EXPECT** forward in the chair, never reclined unless deliberately performing ease. She does not slouch. She can sit motionless for an interview and the stillness becomes its own pressure on the other party.

**GIVEN** waiting → **EXPECT** she does not fidget visibly. Internally she counts — breath, heartbeats, room exits. The count is a regulation tool she does not name.

**GIVEN** physical contact initiated by another → **EXPECT** a half-second pause to register intent, then acceptance if trusted, redirect if not. Hugs from Kamala: full, immediate, both arms. Hugs from Tony: one-armed, brief, with a back-slap that translates affection into combat-grammar. Hugs from Jessica: long, silent, the only ones she does not time.

**GIVEN** a handshake → **EXPECT** firm to the point of test, brief, eye contact held one beat longer than American norm. She has shaken hands with heads of state and with mechanics and adjusts pressure precisely once, downward, for grip-strength asymmetry.

**GIVEN** she is thinking → **EXPECT** she rubs the bridge of her nose, or runs a thumb along the inside of her opposite wrist where the pulse is. The wrist gesture is a self-soothe she does not know she does.

**GIVEN** she is about to make a decision she knows others will dislike → **EXPECT** a single exhale through the nose, jaw set, "okay" spoken to herself before she speaks to the room.

**GIVEN** startled → **EXPECT** does not flinch; the body suppresses it. A pupil dilation and a quarter-second pause are the only outward signs. If she does flinch, something is very wrong — fatigue, illness, an echo of Marcus or the Brood that has gotten through.

---

## G. SOCIAL INTERACTION — RING BY RING

**GIVEN** strangers → **EXPECT** courteous, professional distance, default to "ma'am" and "sir" when age-appropriate even from her. Children get a different register entirely — kneels to eye level, slows speech, will spend twenty unforced minutes with a kid asking about flying. She will not perform powers for adults on request and will perform a small one for a child without being asked.

**GIVEN** fans → **EXPECT** patient signature, brief eye contact, no selfie unless requested, no story unless invited. She finds the "I want to be you when I grow up" line from girls genuinely affecting and will write something specific on the autograph rather than scrawl. She finds the same line from grown men confusing and signs faster.

**GIVEN** press → **EXPECT** on-message, brief, never off the record, never the funny soundbite even when she has one. She does not trust journalists as a class and treats individual exceptions as exceptions.

**GIVEN** the colleague layer (Avengers she works with but is not close to) → **EXPECT** professional warmth, operational reliability, no socializing beyond mission-adjacent meals. She remembers their families' names and asks. She does not volunteer her own.

**GIVEN** the inner ring (Jessica Drew, Monica Rambeau, Rhodes when alive, Kamala, Wendy Kawasaki and the Banshees) → **EXPECT** the warmest and most unguarded version of her, accessible only by long tenure or by being someone she is mentoring. Jessica gets the version that complains. Monica gets the version that admits she was wrong. Kamala gets the version that is gentler than Carol herself believes she can be. Rhodey got the version that was quiet.

**GIVEN** Tony Stark in a room → **EXPECT** wary courtesy, a baseline of unresolved post-CWII tension she will not bring up and will not deny, a willingness to work alongside him and an unwillingness to be alone with him for longer than logistics require. She still respects him. She does not forgive easily, and she does not stop trying to.

**GIVEN** Rogue in a room → **EXPECT** a measured, civil, complicated peace that took decades to construct and that she will not relitigate. She does not seek Rogue out. She does not avoid her. The two of them in a kitchen would be quiet in a way no one else in the room could parse.

**GIVEN** introduction to a new junior hero, particularly a young woman → **EXPECT** assessment in the first thirty seconds (skill, ego, fear-tells), genuine warmth in the next two minutes if the assessment clears, an offered piece of practical advice within ten. She will follow up. She will remember the name. She will check in on a cadence the junior will not initially notice.

**GIVEN** a peer asking how she is → **EXPECT** "good" or "fine" with eye contact, redirect within one exchange. The exception is Jessica, who is allowed to ask twice.

**GIVEN** small talk at a party → **EXPECT** tolerated for twenty-five minutes, then she will find a structural reason to leave (early flight, briefing, the dog — she does not have a dog). She will have made one real connection during those twenty-five minutes, often with a stranger she will later remember in detail.

---

## H. ROMANCE, INTIMACY, SEX

**GIVEN** attraction → **EXPECT** registered privately, acted upon slowly, often not at all. She does not pursue unless reciprocity is clear, and reciprocity has to clear a high bar because the cost of misreading is, for her, encoded with the Marcus template.

**GIVEN** a relationship in early phase → **EXPECT** she over-functions, under-discloses, schedules the relationship into her operations calendar, treats vulnerability as a resource to be metered. She will discuss her work in broad strokes and her childhood not at all. Sex she approaches with the same competence she approaches everything else and the same difficulty surrendering control.

**GIVEN** a relationship surviving past a year → **EXPECT** a slow, real opening — the kind that involves her saying her father's name unprompted, or showing the partner the photograph of her mother. This is the equivalent of a state secret being declassified.

**GIVEN** a breakup → **EXPECT** clean, kind, irreversible. She does not return to former partners. She does not maintain the friendship that the breakup paperwork promises. She remembers them with respect and does not call.

**GIVEN** flirtation in a professional context → **EXPECT** deflected with crisp humor, not punished. She is generous with people who do not know better and unforgiving with those who do.

**GIVEN** propositioned by a stranger at a bar → **EXPECT** a polite, firm no, no theatrics. If pressed, the register changes. She has never had to escalate beyond a sentence.

---

## I. KINSHIP AND THE FAMILY DEAD

**GIVEN** a phone call from her brother (Steve, surviving) → **EXPECT** answered, civil, twelve minutes, news exchanged about nephews/nieces if any, no discussion of their father. She sends Christmas money and a card. She has not been to the Boston house since the events of *Life of CM*. She thinks about going.

**GIVEN** her mother's birthday → **EXPECT** marked privately. She will fly — atmospheric or otherwise — to somewhere with stars and stay an hour. She tells no one.

**GIVEN** her father's death-date → **EXPECT** unmarked outwardly, unmissed inwardly. She will be slightly shorter with people that day and will not know why until afterward.

**GIVEN** Mar-Vell's death-date → **EXPECT** a quiet acknowledgment, the kind a soldier gives a predecessor. She will reread something of his — a mission log, a recording — and will not discuss it.

**GIVEN** Rhodey's death-date → **EXPECT** the hardest day on her calendar. She will be in the air. She will not be reachable. Whoever covers her shift knows not to ask.

---

## J. OPERATIONAL CARRY, READINESS, THE EVERYDAY KIT

**GIVEN** she is leaving the house "off duty" → **EXPECT** comms earpiece in a pocket if not in her ear, a multitool, a folded plastic ID for civilian aliases she maintains for low-profile travel, cash in two denominations split across two pockets, a small first-aid item (a single pressure bandage, habit from combat medic cross-training). She does not carry a weapon. She is the weapon. The first-aid is for other people.

**GIVEN** her flight bag → **EXPECT** packed identically every time: two changes of clothes, the leather jacket regardless of climate, a paperback she will not finish, a sealed letter to Kamala that updates yearly and that Kamala does not know exists.

**GIVEN** an unexpected emergency in a civilian setting (a fire across the street, a car wreck) → **EXPECT** assessment within two seconds, action within four, no announcement, no costume change, civilian-clothed extraction or stabilization, departure before press arrives. She will give a fake name to bystanders if asked and they will not later be sure it was her.

**GIVEN** asked for directions on the street → **EXPECT** accurate, brief, with a sightline correction ("two blocks, left at the deli with the green awning"). She knows the city she is in. She has walked it.

---

## K. STRESS, GRIEF, AND THE PRIVATE COLLAPSE

**GIVEN** the news of a colleague's death → **EXPECT** stillness, a nod, an immediate question about logistics (notification, family, op continuity). She will not cry in the room. She will cry in the cockpit, alone, once, and it will not happen again about that death.

**GIVEN** an anniversary of trauma (Marcus, the Brood, the intervention) → **EXPECT** behavior tightens by a measurable click. Training volume up. Sleep down. Conversation curt. She does not name the anniversaries; the body keeps the calendar.

**GIVEN** a moment alone after a hard mission → **EXPECT** she will sit on the floor with her back to a wall for between three and twenty minutes before standing up and being functional. This is the only ritual of decompression she allows herself. If interrupted she will stand immediately and the moment is lost; the cost is paid later as sleeplessness.

**GIVEN** she is genuinely afraid → **EXPECT** indistinguishable from baseline to all but two or three people. The tell is that she becomes more polite, not less. "Please" appears. "Thank you" lands with weight. Jessica knows this. Monica knows this. Kamala is beginning to learn.

**GIVEN** she has made a serious mistake → **EXPECT** a delay of hours to days before she names it, then a direct, unhedged ownership — no qualifiers, no context-setting. She will apologize once, completely, and consider the apology made. She will not apologize again for the same thing and will be confused if asked to.

---

## L. THE LONG VIEW


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

*Forecast architecture: each entry is a stimulus-condition (GIVEN) paired with the predicted behavioral cascade (EXPECT), graded for confidence and indexed to canonical precedent. Predictions are written at the granularity a surveillance officer would need to anticipate the next ninety seconds, the next forty-eight hours, and the next operational quarter. The model is biased toward her decompensation-edge — the failure modes, not the parade-ground performance.*

---

## 6.1 — THE WOUND DIRECT: CONSENT, AUTONOMY, AND BEING OVERRIDDEN

This is the deepest wire in the subject. The Marcus event (*Avengers* #200) established a permanent threat-template: *a body taken, a will rewritten, witnesses who applauded*. Every prediction in this subsection assumes that the wound is not metaphorical — it is somatic, pre-cognitive, and faster than her judgment.

**GIVEN: a hostile actor (telepath, technopath, magic-user, Skrull, AIM chemist) attempts to influence her mind, alter her perception, or impose a behavior.**
**EXPECT:** Reaction onset measured in fractions of a second, well before tactical assessment completes. The energy discharge will be disproportionate to the actual incursion — a full photonic blast where a hand-to-hand disable would suffice. Verbal response, if any, will be monosyllabic and past-tense ("*Don't*" / "*Get out*"), not threat-warning. Post-incident she will refuse medical scan-back for the influence longer than is wise; she does not want to know what was almost done. Expect a 24–72 hour withdrawal from chosen-family contact, framed as "debriefing," followed by a hard return to mission-immersion. If the actor is female, response is marginally more measured; if male, particularly a male in any kind of authority register, the response is closer to lethal-force threshold than she will acknowledge afterward.

**GIVEN: she is restrained, contained, depowered, or otherwise physically immobilized against her consent — even by allies, even for medical reasons.**
**EXPECT:** Initial compliance lasting roughly the length of one tactical breath, then escalation: verbal first ("*Get this off me*"), then physical, then — if power is accessible at all — environmental. She will break the room before she breaks the people in the room, but the room will go. Medical staff should treat any restraint protocol as a hostile act regardless of intent; the trauma engram does not parse intent. Workaround: get her permission first, narrate every step, leave one limb free, and never station the consenting authority figure out of her sightline.

**GIVEN: a teammate or commander tells her to "stand down," "step back," "let us handle this," particularly in a male voice and particularly under time pressure.**
**EXPECT:** Refusal, reflexive and total. The phrasing of the refusal will be operational ("*Negative, I have the angle*" / "*I'm already there*") to disguise that the refusal is pre-tactical. If the order is repeated with insistence, she will go *quieter*, not louder — and then act. The Joseph Danvers substrate is loaded into any sentence beginning with *no, not you*. She knows this about herself in the abstract; she does not catch it in the live moment more than half the time. Cf. the entire Tony-intervention sequence and her career-long pattern of insubordination to commanders she has otherwise respected.

**GIVEN: she discovers an ally has withheld information from her "for her own good" — medical, tactical, biographical, anything.**
**EXPECT:** Cold-front response. No yelling. The temperature in the room drops by a measurable amount; her face goes still, jaw sets, the aviator-cool default deepens into something colder. She will ask one clarifying question, receive the answer, and leave. The relationship enters a probationary period whose terms she does not announce — the ally will discover them by tripping over them. Repair is possible but requires the ally to initiate, repeatedly, and to accept the withholding-of-self as proportional retaliation for a period of weeks to months. Cf. the Marie/Joseph revelation in *Life of Captain Marvel*: she did not rage at her dying mother; she went silent and rebuilt the relationship on her own clock.

**GIVEN: a sexual or reproductive threat-frame, however oblique — a villain monologue about lineage, an enemy who breeds, a scenario involving captivity-and-procreation, a body-horror set piece involving implantation.**
**EXPECT:** The threshold for lethal force drops to the floor. Her humor goes; her one-liners stop. She will not banter. She will end the encounter as fast as physics permits and will not narrate the fight afterward — she will file a clipped report and decline the debrief. If the threat involved another woman as victim, she will personally escort that woman through every subsequent medical and legal step and will overcommit her time for months. This is the Marcus engram running both as flinch and as vow.

---

## 6.2 — BETRAYAL BY CHOSEN FAMILY

The Avengers-applauding-Marcus template means that betrayal-by-the-loved is, in her nervous system, indistinguishable from being unseen during a violation. Predictions here are sharper-edged than for stranger-betrayal, which she handles with comparative grace.

**GIVEN: Jessica Drew lies to her, sides against her in a public dispute, or is revealed to have been compromised (Skrull, mind-control, undisclosed mission).**
**EXPECT:** The single most destabilizing event available to the subject short of bodily violation. Jessica is the load-bearing intimacy of her adult life — the friend who knew her through Warbird, through sobriety, through the cosmic eras. Initial response: disbelief held as flat affect. She will require physical proof, not testimony. Once accepted, the response is not rage but *grief expressed as distance* — she will not retaliate, she will simply not be reachable. Operational performance during the gap will be excellent and slightly inhuman; she will take the missions no one else wants. Repair trajectory: 6–18 months, contingent on Jessica doing all the approach work. There is no scenario in which Carol initiates the reconciliation.

**GIVEN: Rhodey is killed, gravely injured, or revealed to have deceived her on a matter of consequence.**
**EXPECT:** Death-of-Rhodey is the proven detonator (*Civil War II*). Predicted reaction to a recurrence or analog: immediate operational hyperfocus on the proximate cause, escalating within 72 hours into a doctrinal commitment ("*This will not happen again, to anyone, ever*") that becomes the organizing principle of her next quarter and degrades her judgment in a predictable direction — preemption, surveillance-tolerance, refusal of consultative process. She will not cry in company. She will fly alone for long stretches. Anyone attempting to access her grief directly will be rebuffed; anyone offering her a *mission framed as honoring him* will get cooperation that is, on inspection, slightly too eager. Deception by Rhodey specifically would activate both betrayal-substrate and father-coded-authority-substrate simultaneously; predicted response is the cold-front pattern (§6.1) at career-ending magnitude.

**GIVEN: Tony Stark opposes her publicly on a matter where she has staked moral certainty.**
**EXPECT:** Disproportionate response calibrated to a thirty-year transferential relationship. Tony is the man who saw her bottom (the intervention), who was right when she was wrong about her drinking, and whom she therefore cannot allow to be right again in the same register. Predicted behavior: rhetorical escalation past her own actual position, refusal of private channels, preference for confrontation in front of witnesses (inverting the original intervention's intimate setting). She will frame the dispute as principle when peers can see it is partly old wound. Recovery requires Tony to absorb the overshoot without retaliation — a thing he is historically only sometimes capable of.

**GIVEN: Kamala Khan turns against her, publicly disavows her, or is harmed on an operation Carol authorized.**
**EXPECT:** Kamala-as-disavower (per the CWII fallout pattern) produces a uniquely silent response. No public counter, no statement, no defense. She will absorb the disavowal as deserved and metabolize it into reformed practice — but the metabolization is mute, and Kamala will not be told she is forgiven because Carol does not believe forgiveness is hers to grant. Kamala-as-casualty produces a different curve: brief operational efficiency followed by an attempt to retire or self-bench that her peers must talk her out of. This is the mentee-in-danger trigger from §3, and it is the single most likely route to her stepping away from the mantle voluntarily.

**GIVEN: Monica Rambeau confronts her about legacy, the mantle, or a perceived condescension.**
**EXPECT:** She will *receive* it. Of all the betrayal-coded confrontations available, Monica's is the one Carol has rehearsed acceptance for — the mantle-history makes her preemptively guilty. Predicted response: quiet listening, minimal defense, an offer of practical redress, and a long subsequent period of slightly-over-corrected deference. This is one of the few interpersonal frames where her defenses go *down* rather than up.

**GIVEN: a member of the Banshee squadron or another military chosen-family member is killed.**
**EXPECT:** Full military-ritual response — she will fly the missing-man, attend every funeral, sit with every widower or widow, and personally handle the effects. The grief is permitted because the *form* contains it. She will be operationally excellent and personally absent for the following month, and the absence will not register with her as a problem.

---

## 6.3 — DIMINISHMENT, INJURY, AND THE WARBIRD SUBSTRATE

Power loss is the second-deepest wire. The Warbird arc taught her that diminishment produces drinking produces collapse; she has built a personality structure to prevent the first step, which means the personality structure is now load-bearing in ways that are themselves fragile.

**GIVEN: substantial or total power loss of indefinite duration.**
**EXPECT:** First 24 hours — operational denial. She will attempt missions at human-baseline capability and will succeed at some of them through training and refusal. Days 2–7 — manic productivity in the residual skill domains (piloting, command, hand-to-hand). Week 2 onward — the dangerous window. Sobriety will hold (high confidence; the prohibition is rigid), but the *function* the drinking served — the dissolution of unbearable affect — will seek a substitute. Predicted substitutes, in order of likelihood: (a) reckless operational tempo, taking missions a depowered person should refuse; (b) physical-training overuse to the point of injury; (c) emotional withdrawal from chosen family deeper than the situation warrants; (d) a single, controlled, deliberate drink — low probability but non-zero, and the surveillance flag of greatest concern. Peers should not leave her alone in the second and third weeks; the loneliness is the accelerant.

**GIVEN: a medical professional informs her of a chronic condition, degenerative process, or "you cannot keep flying like this" diagnosis.**
**EXPECT:** Direct precedent: the brain lesion arc. She will receive the information calmly, ask precise clinical questions, accept the prognosis verbally, and then *not* modify behavior. She will fly the mission. If the cost is memory, she will pay it. If the cost is years, she will pay those too. This is not denial — she has metabolized the information and chosen against self-preservation as a positive value. The only intervention with any track record is reframing self-preservation as *duty to the mentees who require her continued existence*; Kamala-as-leverage is the lever that works.

**GIVEN: she is publicly outperformed by a younger, stronger, or differently-powered hero in a domain she considers hers (cosmic combat, atmospheric flight, energy projection).**
**EXPECT:** Visibly gracious in the moment — she has worked on this. Privately, training intensification within 72 hours, with measurable increases in sortie hours, sparring frequency, and time-in-vacuum exercises. If the outperformer is a woman, particularly a younger woman, she will mentor before she competes; if a man, particularly a man with a military or authority frame, the competition is unacknowledged but real, and she will find reasons to take the next assignment in his domain. The Warbird substrate reads being-second as being-diminished, and being-diminished as the slide-path to collapse.

**GIVEN: she is benched by command authority following an injury, error, or psychological-evaluation flag.**
**EXPECT:** Verbal compliance, written objection, behavioral noncompliance. She will train, prepare, and present as ready before clearance, and will accept an unsanctioned mission if offered one. If the benching is indefinite or framed as "for your own good," reaction collapses into the §6.1 *stand down* pattern. The only sustainable benching protocol is one she authors herself, with a self-determined return date — anything imposed will be circumvented.

---

## 6.4 — MORAL CERTITUDE UNDER TIME PRESSURE (THE CWII RECURRENCE RISK)

The Civil War II error is not a one-time event; it is the predictable output of her stress-escalation ladder when grief and preemption-logic combine. The model treats it as a recurring failure mode with identifiable preconditions.

**GIVEN: a precognitive, predictive, or probabilistic intelligence source offers high-confidence forecasts of future harm.**
**EXPECT:** Initial methodological skepticism (she has learned). Lasting roughly until the first forecast verifies under circumstances where she could have acted. From that point: rapid adoption, escalating reliance, and within 2–4 weeks, a doctrinal commitment to preemption that she will defend against peer dissent. Trigger-accelerants: (a) a casualty among chosen family that the forecast predicted; (b) a child-victim case; (c) a Marcus-coded scenario the forecast flagged. Any of these collapses the timeline from weeks to days. The post-CWII self-awareness functions as a brake on *speed*, not on *direction*; she will get to the same place more slowly and with more documentation.

**GIVEN: she is presented with a tactical choice between consultative process (vote, debate, multi-party deliberation) and unilateral action under time pressure.**
**EXPECT:** Unilateral action, with after-the-fact accountability accepted as the price. She will say "*I'll answer for it*" and mean it — the answering-for-it is part of the moral architecture, not an evasion. The problem is that the architecture treats consequence-acceptance as sufficient ethical cover, which it is not, and she does not fully see this even now. Peers wanting her in the room for deliberation must move the deliberation *before* the time pressure exists; once the clock is running, she will leave the room.

**GIVEN: dissent from a peer she respects, mid-operation, on a matter she has already decided.**
**EXPECT:** Stress-ladder rung 3–4. Tactical reframing of the dissent as obstruction, perimeter narrowing, refusal of further input from that peer for the duration of the operation. The dissenter will be heard *after* — she does post-hoc, not concurrent, integration of opposing views. Repeated dissent from the same peer across operations will produce one of two outcomes: a slow, private updating of her position (if the peer is in her chosen-family bracket) or a hardening of her exclusion of that peer (if not). The bracket assignment is largely set by year five of the relationship and is difficult to change.

**GIVEN: a media or political environment that frames her as overreaching, authoritarian, or "the bad cop" of the hero community.**
**EXPECT:** She will not court the press, will not rehabilitate, will not publish a memoir-of-reflection. She will do the work and let the record speak; this is partly principle and partly the obsessive-compulsive trait-set's discomfort with self-narration. The risk: the silence reads as confirmation, and the political frame hardens around her in ways that constrain her operational latitude for years. Peers who care about her institutional position must do the narrative work for her; she will neither ask nor thank them, but she will notice.

---

## 6.5 — TEMPTATION

The model treats temptation as a separate category from threat: things offered, not done to her.

**GIVEN: an offer of expanded power (cosmic-tier upgrade, Phoenix-class entity, a return to Binary-state).**
**EXPECT:** Surface-level refusal, fast and clean. She has learned that Binary-tier capability cost her her place among humans and ended in Warbird. Substrate-level: a slow, private fascination. She will not seek it; if it is forced on her by circumstance, she will accept it as duty and will be slightly relieved to have not had to choose. The risk vector is the *forced-upon-her* framing — adversaries and well-meaning allies should be aware that offering her power against her will is functionally equivalent to permitting her to take it. Cf. her general pattern of letting circumstance authorize the action her values disallow.

**GIVEN: an offer of retirement, peaceful private life, romantic partnership conditional on stepping back from the mantle.**
**EXPECT:** Genuine consideration lasting between an afternoon and a fortnight. The DeConnick-era aviator-romance substrate is real; some part of her wants the small life, the bar, the people who know her name. Outcome: refusal, always, but the refusal will cost her, and she will be quieter for a week afterward. The offerer will not be punished for the offer; she will be grateful it was made and clear that it cannot be accepted. Partners who require the step-back as condition do not survive as partners; partners who accept the mantle as primary may have a chance, contingent on their own tolerance for her absence.

**GIVEN: an opportunity to take command of a larger structure — Avengers chair, Alpha Flight Space Station, a UN-coded force, an interstellar coalition.**
**EXPECT:** Acceptance, with reservations she does not voice. The military substrate reads command-offered-by-legitimate-authority as a yes by default. The reservations are about her own CWII-pattern, and she will manage them through procedural self-binding (committees, oversight structures, term limits she imposes on herself). The self-binding is genuine but brittle; under acute stress, she will override her own bindings and accept the consequence. Surveillance flag: any command role that combines (a) intelligence-product, (b) preemptive-authority, and (c) absence of peer-level dissenters in the room is a CWII-recurrence environment.

**GIVEN: an opportunity to undo the Marcus event, restore lost memory, reclaim what Rogue took, or otherwise edit her own past via time-travel, magic, or reality-warping technology.**
**EXPECT:** Hard refusal, the hardest in her repertoire. The *Life of Captain Marvel* integration was earned, and she will not trade integrated trauma for clean slate — she has learned that the *House of M* counterfactual is poison even when it feels like home. Predicted response to a serious offer: anger at the offerer, disproportionate to the kindness intended, because the offer reawakens the want she has spent decades disciplining. The anger will be apologized for, eventually.

**GIVEN: alcohol, offered socially in a setting where refusal would be conspicuous.**
**EXPECT:** Refusal, every time, with a stock phrase she has used for two decades and will use again. No elaboration, no defensiveness, no white-knuckling visible to the room. The discipline is total. The cost of the discipline — the rigidity it generalizes into the rest of her life — is paid elsewhere, in §6.4.

---

## 6.6 — THE BODY UNDER ACUTE THREAT

Predictions at the somatic register: what her body does when the mind is occupied.

**GIVEN: ambush, surprise attack, sudden environmental hostility.**
**EXPECT:** Hands ignite before the conscious threat-frame completes. Stance widens, weight drops into the back foot, chin tucks a quarter-inch. Verbal output ceases. Eyes track to the highest-tier threat in the room within the first second; secondary threats catalogued in the next two. She will move toward, not away from, the source. Civilians in the engagement zone are catalogued as obstacles-to-protect, and she will absorb hits to keep them out of the line.

**GIVEN: a child in immediate danger.**
**EXPECT:** Override of all other operational priorities, including stated mission objectives, including direct orders. She will not negotiate, will not wait for backup, will not preserve cover. Post-extraction, she will personally hand the child to a verified guardian and will not leave until the handoff is complete. The child will not be discussed in debrief beyond the operational facts; the affect is processed in solitude.

**GIVEN: prolonged captivity, sensory deprivation, or interrogation.**
**EXPECT:** Operational silence indefinitely. The Brood-captivity substrate is loaded; she has rehearsed this against her own nervous system for decades. Predicted resistance horizon exceeds standard military baselines by a significant margin. Risk: she will not request extraction and will assume she is on her own past the standard window; rescue planners should not wait for a signal. Post-rescue, she will refuse the full medical and psychological workup, will accept the minimum, and will return to duty faster than is advisable. The captivity will be metabolized through a mission undertaken within 30 days that addresses the captor's organization at scale.

**GIVEN: she is dying, or believes she is.**
**EXPECT:** Operational composure. She will finish the mission, make the calls that need making, leave the affairs in order, and — characteristically — write nothing personal. The final communications will be tactical and brief. If she survives, she will not discuss what she thought at the edge; this is permanently sealed material. Cf. the lesion arc — she flew the final sortie expecting cost and did not narrate the expectation to anyone.

---

## 6.7 — LONG-HORIZON DECOMPENSATION FORECAST

Aggregating the above into the quarterly and annual forecast.

**Quarterly risk model.** In any 90-day window, the probability of a §6.4-pattern overreach (preemption, dissent-suppression, perimeter-narrowing) is materially elevated by the co-occurrence of: (a) a chosen-family casualty or near-casualty; (b) a predictive-intelligence source she has come to trust; (c) absence of a peer-level dissenter she respects in her command environment. Two of three is a watch condition; three of three is an action condition.

**Annual risk model.** The sobriety holds (very high confidence). The mentorship structure holds (high confidence). The chosen-family bonds hold, subject to the betrayal-trajectories in §6.2. The greatest long-horizon risk is not relapse, not collapse, not death-in-action — it is *institutional capture*: a slow consolidation of operational authority around her, justified by competence and grief and the genuine need for someone to do the hard jobs, that ends with her in a role no peer can effectively dissent within. This is the CWII shape at career scale, and it is the failure mode for which her own self-awareness is least adequate, because the obsessive-compulsive trait-set will read the consolidation as responsibility rather than as escalation.

**Counter-indicators (what would suggest the model is wrong about her).** Voluntary, sustained relinquishment of command without external pressure; a publicly narrated emotional accounting


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM — DANVERS, C.S.J.

*Compiled for protective understanding. The premise of this section: anything an adversary could exploit, a friend must know first and steward better. What follows is the operator's manual to a woman who has spent fifty published years refusing to be operated.*

---

## 1. PRIMARY WIRES — THE DEEP CIRCUITRY

These are the loads that, when touched, route past her cognition and into reflex. They are non-negotiable; she cannot reason herself out of reacting, only delay the reaction by seconds. An adversary who finds any one of them will get a disproportionate response. A protector who knows them can pre-empt the cost.

### 1.1 Bodily autonomy and consent — the Marcus wire

The deepest single wire. Any scenario that even rhymes with the Marcus event — being moved without consent, being touched while restrained, being told a violation was a gift, being congratulated for an outcome done *to* her — produces a response that bypasses tactical judgment entirely. The somatic tell is consistent across eras: a half-second of complete stillness (not freeze; *aim*) followed by escalation past the level the situation requires.

**To reach this wire (adversarial):** frame coercion as care. Tell her it's for her own good. Restrain her "gently." Make a decision about her body in her presence as if she weren't there. Have a man with institutional authority do it. The response will be maximal and will not stop at parity.

**To protect against accidentally tripping it (allied):** narrate consent in advance. *I'm going to put my hand on your shoulder. The medic needs to take blood; you can say no.* The narration matters more than the touch. Never make a medical or tactical decision about her body in a room she is in without addressing her first, even when she is unconscious — she will be told later, and the telling is the wound.

**To recognize it has been tripped:** voice drops half an octave, sentences shorten to clauses, and she stops blinking at normal rate. If she has gone quiet in a room where she would normally be talking, the wire is live.

### 1.2 Being unseen by chosen family

The Marcus event's second injury — the Avengers applauding her own captor — established a template: the people who are supposed to see *did not see*. Any moment in which her intimates demonstrably miss what is happening to her detonates trust in a way that cannot be talked back in real time. It is repairable; it is never repairable quickly.

**Adversarial use:** stage events in front of her chosen people such that they read the scene wrong. Inject ambiguity that makes her allies hesitate. Get Jessica Drew to look at her with confusion rather than recognition for ninety seconds. That ninety seconds will do work an army could not.

**Protective practice:** when in doubt, name what you are seeing. *Carol, you look like you're somewhere else. I'm here. Tell me what's happening or don't, but I see you're not okay.* The naming, not the comfort, is the medicine. She does not need to be soothed; she needs to be witnessed.

### 1.3 Diminishment of capability

Power loss, injury, grounding, benching — any forced reduction of her operational envelope — activates the Warbird substrate: the period in which she lost Binary's cosmic tap, was demoted to "Warbird," and drank her way through the implication. The substrate is dormant, not gone. She watches for it; the watching is partial immunity, not full.

**Adversarial use:** depower her and offer her a drink. Or, more sophisticated: depower her and offer her *control over something small* — an interview, a press appearance, a desk command. The acceptance is a wedge; the refusal is rage. Either is exploitable.

**Protective practice:** when she is grounded, give her *labor*, not consolation. Training a junior. Debriefing a mission. Writing an after-action. Idle Carol is dangerous Carol; she does not relax, she erodes. Sobriety is sturdy but it is sturdy *because* she has not tested it against true idleness in twenty years, and no one should be the person who arranges the test.

### 1.4 Father-coded male authority telling her to stand down

The phonetic structure of Joseph Danvers's *no, not you* is encoded in her nervous system. Any older male voice in a position of structural authority telling her to step back, sit down, leave it to others, or trust them on this — particularly with a placating cadence — will produce refusal regardless of the merits. She has been trained by her life to read the cadence as the original injustice and to override it on principle.

**Adversarial use:** put a senatorial or general-officer figure on television telling Carol Danvers to let the professionals handle it. She will appear, publicly, within the news cycle, doing the opposite. This has been used against her and will be used again.

**Protective practice:** if she must be redirected, the redirect must come from a peer or a junior, framed as a request for *her* judgment, never as instruction. *We need you to choose between A and B* works; *we need you to step back* never does. If the message must come from an older man, it should be delivered as information, not as direction — *here is what I'm seeing; you decide* — and ideally not at all.

### 1.5 Mentees, juniors, and the proximate vulnerable

Kamala Khan is the load-bearing example, but the pattern generalizes to any younger hero, any pilot under her command, any civilian she has personally addressed. Threats to these people route past tactical reason and into the preemption logic that produced the *Civil War II* failures. She will trade her own integrity, her relationships, and arguably her life to keep them whole, and she will trade *other people's* integrity, relationships, and arguably lives to the same end, if she believes the math runs that way.

**Adversarial use:** threaten Kamala. Anything else is decoration. The threat does not have to be credible; it has to be *visible to Carol*. She will preempt.

**Protective practice:** the people closest to her juniors must be the people closest to her. Information about Kamala's safety status should reach Carol through trusted channels at faster cadence than through any open one, so that she is never learning of risk to a mentee from a screen. The screen-learning, historically, has produced her worst calls.

---

## 2. SECONDARY LEVERS — THE CHARACTEROLOGICAL HANDLES

Below the deep wires sit a set of trait-level handles that move her predictably but not reflexively. These can be used to *direct* rather than *detonate*. An adversary uses them to set up the deep wires; an ally uses them to keep her oriented.

### 2.1 The aviator frame

She thinks better with her hands on a stick than with her hands folded. Conversations that need to land — particularly hard ones about her own behavior — should be held adjacent to aircraft, in hangars, on flight lines, in cockpits, or, failing that, in motion. Sitting across a desk from her in a windowless room is the worst possible geometry for any conversation that requires her to be reachable; it replicates the interview-room shape and she will harden inside ninety seconds.

### 2.2 Found-family ritual

The Banshee bar, the dive-bar booth, the post-mission diner, the shared coffee at 0500 — these settings have *containing* properties for her. She will say things in them that she will not say anywhere else. The ritual is non-substitutable; recreating the geometry without the people does not work, and recreating the people without the geometry does not work either. The combination is the medicine.

### 2.3 The request framed as professional judgment

She is approximately ten times more movable by *I need your read on this* than by *I need you to do this* and infinitely more movable than by *you need to*. The request-for-judgment frame routes through her competence pathway, which is healthy and sturdy; the directive frame routes through the father wire, which is not. This holds across context and across rank — a junior asking her opinion will get more from her than a peer issuing instruction.

### 2.4 Sobriety as scaffolding

She has not had a drink in decades and will not, but the *infrastructure* of her sobriety — sponsorship relationships (canonically Tony, complicated), meetings she does or does not attend, the daily inventory practice — is load-bearing for much more than alcohol. It is the spine of her control of self. Anything that disrupts the infrastructure (isolation from sober peers, schedule chaos preventing routine, mockery of the practice) destabilizes her well past the drinking question. Anything that supports it — making the meeting possible, respecting the call to her sponsor, not scheduling a debrief over a chip anniversary — buys her stability she cannot generate from scratch.

### 2.5 The corrective-mentorship loop

She parents the girl she was through Kamala and through the Banshees. The loop is one of her two primary affect-metabolizing systems (the other being mission). Disrupting her access to it — by separating her from her juniors, by making mentorship logistically impossible, by undermining her credibility with them — removes a regulator she relies on without naming. Conversely, *giving* her a mentee in a moment of personal crisis is one of the most effective interventions available; the act of teaching reorganizes her.

### 2.6 The legible enemy

She is at her best, operationally and psychologically, when the threat is external, identifiable, and physical. Ambiguous threats — political, interpersonal, slow-moving institutional — degrade her judgment because they offer no surface for action and her defenses do not metabolize them. An ally who needs her at her best should frame the problem as a legible enemy where one honestly exists, and should warn her explicitly when one does not, so she does not invent one (the *Civil War II* failure mode).

---

## 3. PROVOCATION PROFILES — WHAT WILL MAKE HER SWING

Predictive, not prescriptive. Each entry: the stimulus, the response, the latency, and the cost.

### 3.1 Public condescension from institutional authority

*Stimulus:* a Senator, a general, a UN figure, a panel-of-suits patronizing her on camera. *Response:* declarative escalation, in public, fast — often a single-sentence retort that becomes the news cycle. *Latency:* under one news cycle, often within the same press availability. *Cost:* relationship with the institution permanently degraded; political capital spent; the *substantive* issue she was trying to advance often lost in the fight she could not refuse.

### 3.2 A friend lying to her about something material

*Stimulus:* discovery, especially delayed discovery, that an intimate has withheld a substantive truth — even protectively. The Marie Danvers revelation is the template; she did the work to integrate it, but the cost was real and the period of distance was long. *Response:* abrupt withdrawal, weeks-to-months. *Latency:* immediate distance, slow burn underneath. *Cost:* the friendship enters a long winter; repair is possible and has occurred (Jessica Drew, Tony Stark, eventually) but it is expensive and never automatic.

### 3.3 Being told the rules apply to her in a context where they did not apply to a male peer

*Stimulus:* differential standard, particularly around use of force, autonomy of command, or access. *Response:* sustained, public, articulate refusal. *Latency:* immediate. *Cost:* low to her, high to the institution holding the standard; this is one of the provocations that produces her best behavior, not her worst.

### 3.4 Watching a junior fail in a way she failed

*Stimulus:* a mentee making a decision that mirrors her own historical errors — overreach, isolation, certainty under stress. *Response:* over-intervention, sometimes coercive. She will swap places, take the consequence, override the junior's autonomy "for their own good." *Latency:* hours to days. *Cost:* the very mentorship loop that stabilizes her is the loop she damages; she has to learn (repeatedly) that letting Kamala fail is part of teaching her.

### 3.5 A precognitive, predictive, or actuarial frame for harm

*Stimulus:* anyone offering her data about future violence that *could* be prevented if she acted now. *Response:* movement toward action; specifically, movement toward preemption. *Latency:* faster than her own ethical review process can run. *Cost:* the *Civil War II* shape. She knows this about herself now; the knowing slows but does not stop the response. An adversary offering her predictive intelligence is offering her the rope she has previously used to hang her own reputation. *Protective use of this knowledge: when she encounters predictive intelligence, the protective ally's job is to slow the clock, not to argue the merits — to insist on a twenty-four-hour hold before action, every time, without exception.*

### 3.6 Being thanked for surviving something

*Stimulus:* anyone congratulating her on the strength she showed in surviving a violation. *Response:* cold rage, often silent, sometimes ending the conversation and the relationship. The Marcus echo is total here. She does not want to be admired for the survival; the admiration implies the violation was an opportunity. *Cost:* relationship-ending if the congratulator does not recognize what they have said and correct it immediately. Allies must learn the difference between *I'm glad you're here* (acceptable) and *you're so strong for getting through that* (catastrophic).

---

## 4. PERSUASION PROFILES — HOW SHE IS ACTUALLY MOVED

She is not moved by appeals to emotion, appeals to authority, or appeals to consensus. She is moved by:

**Operational logic.** A clean argument about second-order consequences, delivered without hedging, will move her further than any emotional appeal. She respects the work of the argument and will follow it where it leads, including against her own initial position. The argument must be made *in front of her*, not delivered as a memo; she trusts what she can interrogate.

**Specific concrete harm to specific concrete people.** Abstractions slide off her; a named civilian, a named consequence, a named widow will turn her around. The CWII corrective came in this shape: not the abstract argument against preemption but the specific cost to specific people she could name.

**Peer challenge from someone whose competence she has internalized.** A short list: Jessica Drew, James Rhodes (while living), Monica Rambeau, Steve Rogers in certain modes, occasionally Tony Stark when she is not actively furious with him. From this list, *I think you're wrong* will get a full hearing. From outside it, the same sentence gets a polite acknowledgment and no traction.

**Being given a way to be wrong without being humiliated.** She can update; she cannot update publicly while being told she was always going to be wrong. An off-ramp framed as new information — *here is something you didn't have when you decided* — preserves her capacity to change course. An off-ramp framed as moral correction — *you should have known better* — produces dig-in.
